Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and are treated by division as we have said, but it is unhelpful, then make cauteries: 3 on the spine of the back, that which is completely cut under the armpit little by little in a triangle shape, and 1 cautery under the arm. 2 fingers;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think his stomach is cold and the food is not digested, and one sees the face swollen, then to the face make 1 large cautery on the stomach, as it is said before, and 1 on the liver, and 1 on the spleen with a long cauterizing tool; and leave the cautery in place for a long time. After that, treat the area until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy growth called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you apply the cautery, heat it until it looks like a razor, and then place it directly on the shaven skin; hold your hand so that the cautery reaches the vein's opening, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of skin, cauterize each one as we have said; after this, treat the wound with healing ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the scrotum, it will provide greater relief.
de plaie mal curee	from wounds that were not properly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or opening, as we will describe in its place, then such a disease comes that it cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a patient has an ulcer that is suppurating and oozing pus and corrupted moisture, you should first examine it thoroughly and determine how deep the ulcer is. Then heat the cautery until it looks like a razor and insert it into the ulcer according to its depth, and repeat this process with the cautery one, two, or three times according to its needs; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are nearby, and large veins. If the ulcer goes deep into the bladder and intestines, be careful of these areas, and do not apply the cautery directly to bones, and think that it is not sensible. After treating the area until it is healed, if the wound is still oozing pus, know that it is not fully healed; and if the pus is not draining, know that the bone at its base is affected and corrupted. Then proceed as instructed for such cases.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain comes from cold and is accompanied by strong winds, and does not subside in a woman, then you must apply cautery to the kidneys on both sides using the chisel cautery that we mentioned earlier. If we cauterize it in the middle, there will be .iij cauteries in a row, and they will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and flaccid due to cold and moisture, and the patient retains urine, then you must apply cautery to the part above the bladder where the hairs of the pubic region begin, with one cautery on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the nail of a thumb. And you will do one cautery above the back, or two if you see the need; and the cauteries should be chisel-shaped as described earlier.
de la marris	of diseases
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the disease is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupt and their terms late; and when they come, they feel great pain: then one should make 3 cauteries around the womb, as we have said in the cautery for the bladder, and 2 cauteries on the back; and let the cauteries be on the clavicle, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistors descend to the box of the hip, and due to this they move out of their place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the places of the departure are hollow, then one should cauterize the patient on the box of the hip with 1 cautery resembling a circle, and sign before the place around the box as it turns, so that the box is within the circle; and let the cautery be like those by which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available to you, then make three large cauteries from the olive tree, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the sores; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain arises in the hip joint due to cold and moisture, and the disease is chronic and resistant to the treatments mentioned earlier, then you must purge the patient of the gross humours with foul-smelling pills or similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that, apply cautery; and there are two ways of applying cautery: with burning medicines or with fire. Fire cautery has many methods, one of which is to cauterize the hip joint with three triangular cauteries according to this shape, making a deep and large wound, with the space between each cautery the size of a thumb; the cauteries should be made from olive wood. Another method is to make a cautery in the centre of the hip joint, so that there are four cauteries according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, the cautery with the circular cauterizer that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circles contain the entire hip, and all the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the way one proceeds in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip and does not reach the thigh or leg. And if it reaches the thigh and leg, one makes .2 cauterizations where the patient feels the pain, one cauterization where the pain holds, and another cauterization above the ankle joint on the left side a little; and let the cautery be with a knife, burning through the thickness of the skin. And if the patient feels that the pain extends to two or more places in the foot or nearby, then cauterize there where they feel the pain .3 or 4 times using the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, make more; and if he feels that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make the cautery with a knife or circularly, and take good care in all your cauteries not to leave the cautery on so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who have had cautery performed on the ankle of the foot, and they left it until the leg was completely swollen, and the feet as well, and it was pierced and corrupted throughout the foot. After that, he died from a rupture in his abdomen.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two parts together, do cautery on one and then the other according to this method. // And the wise men said about the cautery of the hip, of which here is the manner: make a iron rod as thick as a thumb, or a little less, and it should be notched all around with notches spaced out by the amount of a finger joint; and the notches should be on both sides, and they should also be like fingers, and there should be a handle made well. And this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it should be heated until it is all red and glowing, and then one should place it on the joint of the ill hip, and turn it onto the healthy side; and the cautery iron should be used once with one cautery rod and left for three days. Then make a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the application of ointment as long as it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its sight, and we see few who use it; and yet it is one of the good cauteries, which those who can bear it should use where it is needed.
de la dolor dou dos	of pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes in the back, from sitting or impact or from excessive evacuation, or by similar appearances of cold matter, none of these appearances are worth cauterizing except for that which comes from the diffusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is fitting, after the patient has been purged with foul pills or similar remedies, that one should make three marked lines on his back where the pain is located, and in each line .v. cauteries or more according to the strength and amount that the patient can endure; and the cauteries should be performed according to the cautery called "the point"; and if you wish, perform .iij. cauteries or .iiij. with the medium cautery needle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight back when they wake up, and fear; and you find it in the last vertebrae of the back, and in us it appears on the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see one and see it treated, then cauterize it with a cautery of celery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	The purple cautery colors every part of the spine evenly. And if you see it, cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery .ij or .iij lines apart, and let the points be close to each other. After that, cure the site until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to use cautery on any swelling that is in a nerve ganglion.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pains are from moistors that are spread throughout the body's limbs, and when pain comes in the feet, which they properly call "podagra," and when it is from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicine, then it is cured by cauteries in this way: make the mouth of the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-colored according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is a need for you to prick the sole of the foot, do cauterization with the entire cautery that is called "point." And if pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, do cauterization on each knee with 3 or 4 cauteries in each part, with all the olive cautery; and if you need more, then do more, but don't hold your hand there longer than until the thickness of the heart is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains go down to the knees and back, administer the cautery that we have described in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, prick around the wrist for 2 lines; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, then prick on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the armpits or shoulders, cauterize each part, and make good treatment for the patient and take medicines. For if you make good treatment for him and purge phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the root of the ulcer
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the ulcer comes in wounds, and the bowels descend to the testicles and it is new, then when you see him being treated, he should not eat that day; and he should use things that loosen the belly so that the farts descend from his belly; then make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his armpits so that the bowels are repaired, and bring them back to your fingers, and sign with ointment underneath the ulcer on the bone of the wrist, and throughout a sign that is similar to half a circle on top of the body; then heat the cautery from which this form comes:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	let it grow until it turns white and falls off. Then reset the bones to their place; and the assistant holds his hand so that they do not move back; and work well on the thighs of the patient, and put underneath him a cushion and a servant on each thigh, and another one on his feet who holds his hands; then place the cautery on the affected area all over your palm, and hold it straight and keep it there until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you get to the bone; and be careful that the blisters do not pop when you apply the cautery, so that you do not burn him; and take care that through this the patient does not die or suffer harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And you should know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are useless. And the cautery for children should be subtle according to their size, and for adults it should be as big as their size; after three days, treat the area around the cautery with butter until the scorch mark is removed; then treat it with other ointments until it heals, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days until the wound is well-healed; and his hair should be left to grow for a long time so that the blisters do not pop when he tries to move around.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, if a well-made brace is provided for him, and he wears it for another 40 days; and has good rest, so that he does not move too much and takes care to avoid too much drinking, eating, and loud laughing; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed. And I will now describe the treatment for dislocating his shoulder.
de la routure dou ventre	of the bowels
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they are not growing any more, then do .j cautery of the cautery according to its quantity, and burn the third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients say that one should cauterize it with a four-angled cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but first mark the place of entry and draw a line along the width above the ulcer, and another from above, and hold your hand in the middle of the cauterization throughout. But the first cauteries are lighter and more mild.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to a limb from falling or wounding, and the pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help, then it should be cauterized with a cautery called "point", and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb, its smallness and weakness, and its virtuosity and location of twisting and of its pain. If it is healed from the first cautery, that's good; if not, do another cautery on top of that one, for such a habit is that it should move in the limb nearest to which it is, so you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	from mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Mixing is sometimes helped by cautery with great care, and especially the disease that comes from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it cauterized, take care if the disease is in its early stages, and it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and neither decreases nor persists, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the body, then do 5 cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hairline; and two on the corners, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and let your hand be so that the cautery reaches the bone, and as much as the skin comes out so that the vapors of the thick humors can come out; and cauterize it according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixing is scattered everywhere and it is manifestly losing, then you should cauterize it with those cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery in the navel, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and 6 cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and another one next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are on the lower calf bone, so that you do not burn them; and sometimes do a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and another one on the stomach bone, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more you do cauterization, the more it helps and benefits; and know that the patient does not feel pain from cauterization as a healthy person would, because their body is already completely corrupt. And cauterization should be large or small according to the limbs and joints, depending on how you find them in the methods of iron tools. After treatment, cleanse the site with wheat flour and honey, and other treatments until it heals.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling occurs in a limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices but does not heal, then cauterize the limb according to its size; and let the cautery be slightly warm at the depth of the skin. Then treat it with ointments until it heals. Sometimes cauterization is done on the hand, foot, or back, at the exit point of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; but one should not attempt this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exit points of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of albars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is awakened, and the remedies of medicine are of no avail, then cauterize it with a cautery slightly deep, according to the quantity of the thickness of the skin, so that the whiteness is removed, and its color changed; then cure with flour of beans and lentils, with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of almond, of each one part; and mix all together, and tie it with a cloth, and air in the location until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure for cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When cancer comes at the beginning, and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with a cautery which seems like a circle, all around the cancer. And yet, wise people say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the cancer; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have indeed seen this happen sometimes. A more careful thing is to cauterize all around, with the cautery which is called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot be cured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it is late to die, either because of the superfluity that it causes, or because of the age of the disease when it is decrepit (that is, very old), and he has little blood, or because of the time; and you see him hastening to die: then cauterize him all around with many small cauteries; after that, leave it as it is. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see him piercing throughout the cautery, then heat the cautery tool of which this is the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of the disease called  "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the skin, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels them deeply in such a way that the flow of the pus is relieved. After that, dress the wound until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of disease there is which is called "corroding", and it is nothing other than a corruption of the limb, for it corrupts the limbs just as fire does to dry wood. If you see this disease in a place that can withstand cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries, both large and small, according to what is needed in the place where the disease is; then cauterize all over until you reach the whole corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that all that is corrupted is removed. And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized areas an ointment with oil until the burns from the fire are healed, and all the corruption. After the cure of ointments that generate flesh. And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, that is good; and if not, then restart the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas. And this corruption has sometimes been cured by medicine instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of much greater help, and I have already described the cure for medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of warts that come on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	It often happens that on the feet, through deficiency, there arises a disease which in our opinion is called  "clots", and it is a hard lump that breaks the foot. And the cauteries for this disease are according to two methods. That is, cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water. Cautery with fire is that you heat 1 cautery-iron just like a pen, and it is made of good iron to the size that it can touch the nail all over, and that it has thin edges; then put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; and leave it as such for 3 days so that it starts to produce pus; then make an ointment of mallows crushed with salt, and leave the ointment on all night, and the nail will fall off and be uprooted by its roots. Then cure the place with ointment generating flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by going through the body, and often occur in hands and feet, then you must administer hot-water cautery; and it is in such a way: take an iron or bronze rod, or a pen of vutul, and place it on the nail and the surrounding skin, that is to say, warts; and place the rod so that it covers the entire area, then apply a little warm water, and hold your hand steady, and press your hand as you turn it so that the edge of the rod comes to the root of the nail, and thus find the hot water deeply penetrates to the root; and let the patient endure the bite of the hot water for a while; then leave it thus, and it will be pulled out by its roots. Thus do one after another, until you draw out all those in the body, then cure them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever, or from other causes, then you should do four cauteries, or four on each side of the spine, one cautery between each vertebrae; and one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach with an olive-shaped cautery; thus it will cease the trembling, and hasten the healing from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of foul pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	None appear on the body sometimes but foul pustules, which come from great putrid matters. One should first cauterize at the top of each pustule when they appear, using a thin cautery made from myrtle-wood, with its tip taken to the fire, or long aristolochia root, or lenticular cautery. Sometimes one should cauterize them at their appearance according to this manner, and they cannot grow further from where they came, but the superfluities from which they come are disrupted, and they are healed; however, one must do this after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, you should quickly put your index finger over the wound of the vein and squeeze it hard until the blood is calmed under your finger and no drops come out; then put in the fire olive-wood cauteries, both small and large, as many as are needed, until they are all red; then take .i., either a large or small one according to the wound and where the artery is running, and put the cautery on that vein where you are holding your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bleeds again when you lift your finger off the wound, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another of the cauteries which are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this with one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and beware that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well-stopped immediately if the artery is large, except by one of four methods which we have described: either by cautery, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by strong binding with thread, or by medicines placed on it which have the power to stop bleeding; and it should be bound and compressed skillfully.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies a tight binding with bandages or placing hot things on it, or other similar things, if it does not help then it is no good.Et quant li sans decourt d’une artere qui est petite, et que ne pooit mie estre restenchiee de nule maniere qui nos avons dit, si covient que l’on le fie par medicines qui ont pooir de restenchir; et si le sans decourt d’une artere grasse, si doit il estre restenchiz par liement ou par cautere.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they do not have any mirth or present medicine, then one should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and firmly press until it is constricted above the wound and above the vein; and one should not move it, but moisten it with cold water often so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed and swelled and constricted; and make inquiries beforehand about what they need in terms of cautery and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for wounds:
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every disease that requires cauterization by fire, or burning medicine, and the poultices, causes, instruments, forms of cauteries; and I have covered that chapter from head to foot, and I will continue on the same path in this chapter so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one about cauteries, and therefore one must be more cautious. Car li perils et li paors que on encuntre por les tailles de s’estomache, et les maux que il en advient, si com est la piere, et l’estracions d’elle, et les saings et les maux qu’on encuntre, et les estrumens qui conviennent, et les cauteres.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to be foolish. Because people come to cures in many ways. Some are so worn down by their illness that they would recover quickly if it weren't for the delusions they experience because of their sickness, and the severity of their wickedness; and one must fear these types.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And among these are those who recover their senses and say: "Wait, I am healed"; but the disease is stubborn. You should not consent to those who come to you with such behavior, but place more importance on your honor than on your desires. Act wisely and cautiously in what you know and can prove, and use prophecy and indication in treating your illnesses, for salvation is turned towards these. And this will help you gain a good reputation, glory, and praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, may Our Lord give you wisdom and righteousness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy breath from his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Here I have ordered this chapter in discussing by chapters, according to what it is before the chapter of cauteries, which I have discussed from the head to the feet, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Do you know that this disease often comes to children when they are born, and when the head is squeezed too hard during childbirth; and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in adults, and in all those that I have seen, death has followed; and because of this, it seems better to me to leave the treatment out of such cases.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was filled with water, and his skull grew larger every day until he could no longer support it; and he believed that the moisture would kill him, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone above the brain, between the heart and the bone; and the treatment is such that if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should split a large opening in the middle of the skull; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture runs out; and see the form of spatumile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscesses are larger, then make two slits in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see are the openings of the skull on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand from within, and it has not closed again: then you should split the skull in three places according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, squeeze out all the moisture. After that, bind the splits with bandages and powder, and apply wine and oil, and leave it thus for five days; then loosen it, and cure the wound by tenting and anointing, and let the head be bound tightly, and give the patient dry meat from a pot of moisture as long as the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the abscess opens, and the gathering of fluid; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut where the abscess opens, and the gathering of fluid, and do it according to what you are able; and be careful not to cover the artery; and let blood flow, so that the patient dies from blood loss and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone that they have a disease called "cataract" in their eyes or feet, and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last resort is cauterization with which one will cut open the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	When you see them bending forward, the patient should bend back his head; then rub the area around an artery with a rough cloth until the veins appear, then hold the patient's neck with all your strength using a cloth; then look where the vein is pulsating, and the pulse points are after the ears, and they are barely visible; then sign the pulse points with a cross, then bind both of them with a bandage made from a pointed piece of cloth two parts in width so that the bandage reaches the bone, and this should be done on the side of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, tie the bandage under the artery and over it, cutting also as two parts across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is bound, then the blood flows upwards continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to feel it, then you should measure the amount of space of three inches, then sign inwards and cut to the bone; and what it needs for the blood to flow out is 1/4 cup, and perhaps a little more or less depending on what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then examine the wound: if there remains on the bone no trace of pus, so that no abscesses come from it, then strain the wound and ligate it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	from grain
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old grain comes, and a catarrh occurs, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples, and ancient madness and similar things, and medicine does not help him through various methods of treatment, then we must cut the arteries in the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extraction is for the patient to pull back the hair from his temples, and feel for the artery which opens in the temple, for it will be evident by its pulse, and is not very deep in some people who are too cold; if it is deep, the patient should stretch his neck backward with a cloth, then rub the area with some coarse cloth, and moisten the area with warm water until the artery becomes visible; then take the spatulum, from which comes the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then pull the skin gently until you reach the artery, then pull it upward with tweezers, and separate it well from the layers of tissue beneath; if the artery is thin, then pull it to the tip of the nail, then cut it according to the amount of the .ij chiés (a unit of measurement). For if it is not cut, the blood will not flow properly.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out blood from the vein, just to three ounces; and if the artery is large, then tie it in two places with a strong double thread of silk so that putrefaction does not come before the healing of the wound, and let the blood flow gently; then sop up the excess fluid between the two ties in that same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with an iron cautery to the bone until the shoulder is cut through; and this is the main course of treatment if the patient does not have a fever and is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery helps to finish moistures; therefore it is of greater help for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the wound with old cotton and places on it tents well made; and when they are taken off, they should be treated with dry medicines that cause charring, and with tents until it is healed; and if without cutting into the artery as far as you work, you hasten to cover by cauterization, or you employ vitriol and press it to your hand so that the blood is stanched; and if you do not have that at hand, put on the spot ice as long as the blood stops, and moisten the spot with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and then bind it as tightly as is appropriate; and what is better and easier in the extraction of an artery is to cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery of two parts, but the cutting edge should be well thickened to retain its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And you should have between the two knives a distance of a thumb's width, and then when you have burned in both places, you must put the hot iron on as far as the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and let the two heads be separated because they are not joined by this cautery all over; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears are flowing from the veins that are above the test of the head, and medicine does not help, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel pulsation in the forehead as if from trembling; and if the eyelids are drooping and moist so that the eyelashes have fallen, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called it in the past "crushed cure", and it is that you do to the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has on his forehead, then make .3 incisions on the forehead evenly along its length; and let one of the incisions be as two thumbs altogether in front going down to the nose, and the other .2 at the sides above the eyelids, and keep away from cutting the arteries that are at the sides above the eyelids; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the .2 mandibles, and let each wound be the length of three thumbs across the joints;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	take a piece of sponge and cloth to wipe the blood away, then fill the syringe with two parts of this mixture:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision on the temple all the way to the second incision; and scrape all of the skin in between the two incisions down to the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, then remove this syringe.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	then insert into the first incision the instrument called a «cultellar», which is very sharp on one side and not sharp on the other, and this is how it is shaped:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the cutting edge towards the armpit and the blunt edge towards the bone, and insert it as far as the middle incision. Then compress all of the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it reaches the one that opens from the armpit, and then do the same in the middle incision until it reaches the other one; then draw out the blood evenly, and express the area where the blood was taken; then place a tent made of old cotton in each incision, and moisten it with wine and oil and garlic, and be careful that no pus comes near it; on the third day loosen the ligature, and administer plenty of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment and rose oil, and other treatments for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has chronic cataracts, and you see their eyes are pale and small, and their vision is weakened, and the eyelids burnt, and hairs grow from them, and in their head there is sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; then know from these signs that these substances and this cataract come only from many veins, and the medicine used to treat it is like this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you must command the patient to raise his forehead, then make a large cut through the middle of the forehead, and another from one temple to the other, and let the incision go down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples which cause movement when eating; and when the bone is exposed, you should suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then remove any damaged tissue between the two lips of the cut, and insert old cotton there, and apply tenting with linen; then bind it up with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil, taking care to avoid abscesses; when it is healed, you must rub the bone until new growth begins, then treat it with astringent substances which promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flower, and four parts of colophony, and make an ointment from it; and administer it to the wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear-ach
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains, or insects, or minerals like iron, or similar objects. It could also be fluids like water, or garlic and similar substances.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When a stone or other object that does not adhere to the ear falls into the ear and does not grow in the ear, one should expose the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, apply some violet oil or sisament oil, then extract it with forceps; and cause the person to sneeze with a condiment, and plug the nostrils when the sneezing comes on, and tie a piece of cloth or wool around the ear; and expose the ear to the sun. Often, this will dislodge the object; and if it does not, one should extract it with fine forceps, for which these are the instructions:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it dislodges with forceps, that is good; if not, then extract it with a fine, small pair of tweezers; and if it does not dislodge thus, make an iron hook and insert the tip into the ear canal firmly, and pack wax around the hook so that air cannot enter with the hook; then pull firmly upwards, for often this will work as we have said. And if it does not dislodge thus, take a leech in which to place some instrument made for this purpose, and place a bit of cotton around it; then press the leech against the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not yield to all the things we have said, then hasten to split the ear so that the abscess drains, and there will be a spasm; and the method of splitting is that you first bleed the patient from the head vein, and draw blood according to its strength, then make the patient sit between your hands, and turn his ear upwards, and make a small split in the root of the ear at the fat where it hangs; and let the split be like a crescent moon as you come to the stone, then press it with all your might, and suck it eagerly with your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if there are grains inside and it is swollen, then administer an extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a .i. subtle spatumile according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And administer an incision on that grain. But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract them with subtle pincers and a sucking instrument, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the ache that falls into the ear, the patient should use a first-degree nostrum and dry the ear with old cotton. And let him lie on his side where the ache is. If it yields to this, that's good. If not, take many small stones according to your thumb's thickness, and heat them in the fire; then put one end of the stone into the ear, and press the other end with another stone; and do not stop doing this from stone to stone until all the ache comes out, and so it will all come out; and if you see fit, take a reed, and insert one end into the ear, and heat the other end in the fire until the reed is burnt; then do the same with another reed until all the ache comes out, as we have said for the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In extracting the object from the body, if it is small like a flea or similar, remove it as we have described in the previous section. However, if the object is large enough to be felt, use tweezers for extraction; this method is the most suitable for objects lodged in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When treating earworms, after you have attempted the methods described in the previous section and in the treatment of distilleries, if the cure is ineffective, examine the ear in sunlight; if you see any worms, remove them with fine tweezers. If none are visible, take a small piece of wool and insert it into the ear canal; this will attract and trap the worms.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.
