Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it is narrow below and wide above. Insert the thinnest end of the cotton into the ear according to the degree of discomfort experienced by the patient; then gently suck on the entire piece of cotton, repeating this process until all the worms emerge. If they refuse to come out, pack the ear with cotton as I have described in the section on stones; if they still do not emerge as described, administer distillations that the ancients have found effective in the removal of worms, and you will find them described in the section on distillations. Distill your oils and medicines into the ear through this device, which is crafted as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or brass with a narrow spout and a wider container for distillation; and for pressing the distillation into the ear, use a well-crafted instrument of brass, or take a razor blade and wrap the tip with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and any other medicines, into the cotton, and insert the cotton into the ear. Next, place the razor blade over all the cotton and gently press your hand to temper the heat so that the medicine is distilled into the ear; the patient will feel it working inside, and the distillation should be moderately warm as it enters the ear, but not too hot so that the medicine loses its effectiveness.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear stoppers
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears, and the same thing happens to adults due to stoppers from a wound or something stuck inside the ear. Sometimes these stoppers push inward and become hidden deep within the ear, and sometimes they cause a slight protrusion that can be seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When the stopper is hidden deep within the ear and cannot be seen, it is a difficult condition that can lead to various complications. In such cases, one should expose the affected ear to the sun and examine it closely. If you see the membrane bulging outward, then you must treat it in the following manner:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and pointed both in front and behind, so that it does not pierce the ear. If the stopper is made of matter from the body or ear, then use fine pincers to grasp and gently scoop it out until all the matter is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the obstruction is complete in the ear, take a razor that is thin and light, heat it slightly in the fire, then place it on the body of the ear. If you feel the obstruction which the sick person feels deeply in his hearing, pierce gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a plug according to the size of the aperture, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or take a plug and moisten it in rose water, and powder with vitriol ground; and if you see swelling in the ear, then it is fitting that you pull out the plug and replace it with another plug moistened in cerotum made of olive oil and wax, until the swelling is relieved; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is bleeding, soak a sponge and a cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding that are used for treating distempers.
de la char des papieres	of paper charcoal
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ointment comes in papers when they are moist and dry; you should then extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the tip of a spatula from its roots; then put powdered vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they are without skin, then cauterize them with a thin lens-shaped cautery, and the cautery after the incision helps; and many times they return, as long as something remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times they come in papers from things that look like hail in shape and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hailstone", and it is an assembly of moisture thick in the paper above and below; its work is such: cut first if the hailstone moves from one side to another, and it is a simple thing to know; then open it with tweezers, and pull off the skin. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, it will not harm the patient; and if the split is large, then tie it up, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not force it, for the ointment will heal it at once and prevent infection.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hives are descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then reverse the paper, and press them with tweezers; and if the paper is removed by incision, it does not matter; and when the hives are crushed, wash the area with salted water, and clean the place of that which causes pain until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is woven into papers above, and this happens more to children than to no one, and it hurts a lot in their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten in their eyes; and because of this, they lie on their faces afterwards and sleep on it, and their eyelids are moist, which covers the swelling and appearance with exinach that opens in the eye. And when you press the area with your fingers, you can feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient puts his head on the healthy person; and then take a .i. linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the form of a circle according to the quantity that exinach contains in each part, and then put it over him; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moist skin with a spatular blade, and do not make it any larger than the wound that is made in the healthy vein; and in various dispositions, exinach comes out of the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take therefore a piece of cloth and fold it between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to press into the fracture so that you do not go all the way to the joint, lest you damage it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the bone does not appear at the beginning of the fracture, then push the fracture slightly open until it appears; then extract as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and place on the wound, and apply bandages tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it has a feverish abscess, treat with cooling poultices until it is healed. And if there is a hot abscess at the site, treat with cooling ointments until it is healed.Et s’il vient au leu aposteme frouid, si met sus emplaustre chaut, et li apper en la voix de l’esguiselle, si doit aler a l’esguiselle jusques qu’il soit sanez.
des poilz des papieres	And if it has a cold abscess, use a hot poultice, and if there is swelling in the throat, let him go to the doctor until it is healed.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow from papers, different than their natural state, and they are in a disheveled state, they harm themselves and bring on various diseases, like tears, softness of the papers, and albugine, leading to the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by an aqueous medicine as mentioned before the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by means of canes, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it turns, that is good; if not, insert a needle into the paper at the margin where the hairs are growing, and pass a thread through the paper from top to bottom, and turn it over to the razor; then make an incision in the part under the paper, under the abnormal hairs, starting from the great tear duct up to the small one; then remove the thread, place a small tent of cotton and linen underneath the paper, then mark on the paper a figure according to the amount you want to raise the divided paper.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a need to cut out a large amount of paper according to how soft the paper has become, then make an incision along the two lines you marked, starting from the great tear duct up to the small one; and let one of the incisions be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a hair root, then insert the needle into one of the corners of the wound, then cut it all the way around; then bring together the two lips with a suture of a fine woolen thread through an needle, and wipe away the blood, and apply the surplus threads above the two eyelids to any sticky substance; if not, then do not care about it, then leave the suture and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without a suture using dry and constricting substances, because the paper will reattach itself to the wound and the suture is useless (as the ancients say), and this procedure is done without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if in another way: and it is that you draw the paper with a figure that is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, at .iij. inches apart according to the shape which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is above with small scissors evenly according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the tweezers, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with which to sew it up in the middle of the figure, and another thread through the upper lip, and the second thread through the lower, and bring the threads together evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly and lift off all the skin over which you have signed, as we have recounted, then bring together the two lips of the wound by sewing it up, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes at your incision, then soothe it with cerote and soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes the paper's hair becomes reversed, so you must use what we have said about the incision; but sewing in one and another is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of bones is as follows: fold the parchment and cut it according to what I have said, then make two cannulas as long and as wide as the spatumile; and tie two threads at each end where you hold the threads; then assemble them both subtly above what protrudes from the parchment, and extract the two cannulas from the two ends formed; and leave them thus for several days, and the skin which is being extracted will die and harden and slough off as it falls away.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is slow to heal and the wound still open, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed and the parchment lifted, the hairs will no longer grow. This is the form of the two cannulas that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and breadth:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the procedures are such that you thread a fine needle, and insert a fine silk thread through it; then assemble the threads and tie them together tightly, and let the length of the threads be about the length of a palm; then prepare in the spatumile another fine silk thread, and tie the ends of the thread; then place the patient's head in your hand; and keep it exposed to the sun so that the procedure is not hidden, for this is a subtle and delicate procedure; then insert the needle all the way into the parchment close to the root of the hair, and draw out the hair along with the spatumile until it passes through the parchment, and thread the hair into the spatumile, whether there is one, or two, or three, or more hairs; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out through the spatumile and the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the scrotum is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then you will treat the scrotum underneath to the very end that you have prepared for it, until the scrotum comes out from the opening above and you see it through the eye; then you will treat the scrotum and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, accompany it with a long hair from the horse's mane, and let it grow with that one which you leave, until it lengthens, and then you will pull it.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the pustule of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called 'alacrati' or the pustule comes to the eye, there are two ways it can happen: natural and unnatural. And it happens suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way to treat the natural pustule that comes from the eye is to split the sudore, and loosen its eyelids, and put in there tents of linen, and ligate it until it is healed; and you must not use in its treatment anything that dries and restricts. For if you do this, then the disease will return worse than before; but use things that moisten, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or altus and seed of flax are cooked, and ointments daquilon melted in one of the oils, and wrap it up with a tent, and treat it so.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the goal of your treatment is that you take care that it does not heal according to the form that it was before; and these works which we have said are not effective remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease, which is properly called "axacrati", has natural and accidental causes. The accident comes from wound, incision, cautery, and similar things; and the way to treat it is to take a needle with a double thread and pierce it into the flesh at the corner of the eye, so that the threads come out on both sides, and then the flesh above the needle is cut open, and the cup is spread out by a spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, it is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the slit, turn the paper over, and make 2 slits on each side within the paper; and the edges of the 2 slits on either side of the incision that you have cut, and make angles so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter with the name "J. grische"; then remove the flesh, according to how much it was cut below, from what followed the paper, then join the 2 separated parts, and sew them together with a thread of wool; then treat him with the medicine that softens, and with tents, until he is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a split or stitch or cautery, then you should make a clean split underneath the hair of the scalp, and according to what is written above; then separate between the two lips of the tent, as I have said; and one must perform the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares remedies with all his power so that the shape returns to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what he needs in terms of treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Sudden headache
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this soudure occurs in many people in such a way that the paper above is soaked with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you should therefore insert the point of a razor underneath the paper and lift it up; and use tweezers to hold it, until you pluck out the hairs which are stuck in the spatulum, being careful not to use one that is too sharp or blunt, so that the patient cannot stand the pain of the too-sharp spatulum bleeding the eye; and make your incision, by which you scrape away this blockage, gently, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and all of this assembly is healed, and sometimes in the eye there is a salt water, and it is relieved with sweet water and a compress; then place between the paper and the eye a tent made of linen, and apply to the eye wool soaked in egg white; and after the third day, use the collyrium and soothing remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the fingernail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is in two ways: it is nervous and resembles a hard scurf; and another that is not nervous but resembles congealed white moisture, which when touched with iron and pinched as if with tweezers, feels nothing. Both kinds begin at the inner corner of the eye, growing little by little until they cover the entire sight, light, and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of the incision is that the patient puts his head down, then opens his eyes; and hold the paper in your hand, then grip the nail with small tweezers and pull it up; then take a needle and thread a horsehair, or cow hair, or ox hair through it, doubling over the tip of the needle a little and pushing it all the way through the nail, then tie the nail to the thread and lift it up, then scrape the skin along the side of the nail from the cuticle to the quick, and clip the remainder at the root of the tear duct until you reach the thin membrane beneath, applying gentle pressure and leaving the natural membrane over the tear duct untouched so that the incision does not affect the flow of tears; and sometimes only the cuticle is lifted, along with the thread, as we have said. Then scrape it all along the thin membrane underneath:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful not to touch the fleshy membrane and break it, nor pierce the tear duct; and after the incision, apply a little powdered quicklime to the eye, and a bandage made of linen soaked in vinegar, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push in the needle, and the hook will not go in, many times this appearance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, so work the eye of the patient, and take the spatulum lightly hooked according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently lift the nail, and if you see that it is not lessening and the pus is pressing out, then distil from your mouth into the eye an ointment made of litarge and red copper ore, both ground together, and stop up the eye until the next day; then recommence the other treatment according to this same method, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is nothing contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then milk it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then recommence the treatment as before, until it is healed.Et se li ungles sont lons et i poissent de l’oil, si distille en l’oil coliere fait d’un vairain et de litargire et de sel, et les i estoupe jusc’a qu’ils soient ostes; puis rencomence l’altra ovraige selonc ceste meisme forme.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid harms the eye with great damage, then stop it up with an ointment, and cut away a part but not all of it so that no tear fluid comes; then distil into the eye red ointment made of litarge.And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push in the needle, and the hook will not go in, many times this appearance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, so work the eye of the patient, and take the spatulum lightly hooked according to this form:
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	In some people a red growth sometimes occurs over the pupil, covering it and pressing down on the eyelids, turning them inside out; it resembles a rosebud. The treatment is to have the patient hold his head steady, then open the eye, and cut away all the growth with scissors at an angle suitable for this purpose, and keep up pressure; next cut away the outer growth, working inward little by little until finished, being careful not to injure the eye during the procedure. The incision should be made as described in the section on incisions for nail growths, using gentle force to remove the growth, just as demonstrated in this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is complete and all the growth removed, apply egg white mixed with red vitriol and similar corrosive medicines to the eye, and over that place a piece of cotton impregnated with egg white, so as to protect against hot abscess; if nothing remains, and the white eye membrane is exposed, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with cooling remedies; then return to the treatment until the eye is healed, and thus do for any similar growths.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you should also consider the treatment of weak eyes by natural means, and of accidentally injured eyes by iron working; and do not put your hand to any of these treatments until you see that this member is suffering from that treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of them
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	There are red veins that are covered over the eye, and they harm the sight and weaken the eye all day. Therefore, first, you must examine the eyes to see if there is anything else wrong with them apart from the stye; then treat it in this way: instruct the patient to tilt his head back, then squeeze the veins gently according to his judgment, and let the openings be subtle twice according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two openings by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then squeeze the veins gently, and draw out the blood an hour after another, until you see the veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to hurt the eye with the points of the spatulae, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not touch anything but the veins; and when you have done that, distill into the eye a mixture of green and red to corrupt what is left of the stye.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	If you cannot extract all of this in one hour, then make a poultice from things that soothe the pain of the eyes and leave it for several days until the pain is eased and the abscess is healed, then start again according to the method described above until it is cured; this is the recipe for the ointment:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Examine the "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cautery and medicines that produce heat according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, there will be a wound in it where you must split open the abscess and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and darkness, then remove all of it with an instrument like the one in the current figure; it is called a "rough head" and should be made into a small, pointed tool like a file as shown in the present figure.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on the site of the corrupt bone, then turn it between your fingers and press with your hand a little while until you feel that the corruption has been removed; and do this several times, then restore the site with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the wounds are sewn up and scabs form, and the flesh of the bowels is sewn up, and it remains like this for 40 days, and if it does not heal and there is no sign of improvement, you know that it is healed; if not, then do nothing but pull on the fistula from the opening in the navel according to the following form: and you must uncover the bone a second time with iron and with hot medications, and when it is uncovered take this 3-pointed iron tool, and the staff should be tapered to a point as shown here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone over the ulcer, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then return to pushing the entire tool as far as it can go until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it with every movement, if they hold their hand over their navel; then restore the site with dry medications as I have instructed you, and when the scabs form and harden, they will see that the matter has gone to the navel; this is much easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the opening of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open and there is no disturbance or thinning of the lens, you should bind the patient's eye; then heal it, then place leeches without burning to suck out the blood, then apply a poultice made from acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla on top of the eye, and then compress the eye with bandages and cloth; the way of using the cloth is to take soft cloth and double each one in four, then place them one on top of the other according to the amount that the eye needs; then compress it from above with a firm bandage, and start again with the leeches to suck without burning; then remove the leeches and leave the eye compressed day and night, and if the bandage becomes soft, you should tighten it; then remove the poultice after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, start again with the poultice and bandages until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the rupture of a woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in woven fabric, it opens and reveals something like a resin grain, and it is frightening to see. Therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread in the armhole; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the area of the double thread and tie one part of the fabric tightly, then pull out the needle and place a soft lining on the eye, and leave it until the thread breaks with the fabric, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed. Sometimes the wound is restricted by the fabric in a circular pattern around the wound, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great appearance, then pierce them with a sharp spatulum which comes from the bottom of the eye, and corrects the white moisture and lowers the eyes, and enter in as soon as possible; then extract it until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease, which is called "alcunnati", is only in the bow that is assembled in the eye, resembling a descending water, but it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the treatment is to make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then hold the head between your hands for a while, and move it so that you see the bow coming up to your eyes; then it should be stopped there, and the light should not descend and be obscured, and the patient should see things as he used to. And if it does not go down under, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not apparent as we have said, make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sharp spatulum and press on the white part of the eye  a little bit through the continuation of the conjunctiva with the white part and the cornea, until the bow comes out; and when it is issued, distill into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that has been boiled with honey, then let it be cured with another cure until it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have already discussed the appearance of the diseases in their division, and what should be done to pierce them; now we must act according to health. It is necessary for you to make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light so that he does not see the sun, and press his healthy eye very firmly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your right hand if they are on the right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are on the right; then place the tip of the instrument against the crown by the thickness of a hair at that white part of the eye to the smaller tear duct, then suck the instrument called "almagda" gently, and turn your hand so that it pierces the white of the eye, and you will feel that the almagda reaches the hollow; and the measurement of the path of the almagda should reach the bottom of the space between the pupil and the edge of the iris; this is the crown of the eye; then you will see the bone in this paper due to the clarity of the horny membrane, then place the instrument where the aqueous humor is, then express it beneath one pathway after another. If the aqueous humor flows out now, the patient will see the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a little rest, if the aqueous humor rises again through the second pathway, insert the instrument and when it is stuck and no longer rises, gently withdraw the almagda by turning your hand slightly back and forth; then put in a little more rose oil, and remove this eye from inside. Then place on top of the eye a compress of cotton or wool moistened with rose oil and egg white, and bind it with the healthy eye. We, and those who are of our time, place on top of the eye a poultice of ground eggs with an abundance of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are some people who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so pierce the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep, but make .i. slender incision, then pour in alum, as we have said; and when the work is complete, prepare for the patient .i. dark bed, in which he sleeps on his back in .j. dim place; and he must avoid all movement, and eat light foods, and not move his head or to the right or left, and he should be bound according to his condition for three days; then untie him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then bind the eye again until the seventh day; and you must not do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but you should lighten this, so that the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And if there are hot abscesses, you must untie the eye before the seventh day, and use that which soothes abscesses; and when it is appeased, then untie the sight and put on his face  .i. eyelid to cover some of the eye, and then he should stay in that dark house again. And then leave the house little by little, and return to his usual activities; and know that no disciples should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Yrach, who told us that in his country they pierce with alum, for which they suck out the water, but I have never seen anyone doing this in our land, nor have I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of alchemy, so that those who do not know them can see them; and they should be of bronze properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the heads be of the same subtle material, and the rear ones in three angles sharp.
de la char sor le neis	of the character above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes there are various bumps on the nose; some look like scorpions with feet. And there are some with a blue-colored groove, and some with a light-colored sore. For that which is sore, and not grooved, you must make the patient sit facing the sun; open their nostrils, and spit onto the bumps, and draw them out; then cut what you can sustain with a very sharp, thin knife on one side, as long as you know that the bump is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any part remains that cannot be covered, open it with a subtle, light instrument, so that nothing remains; and if without swelling, or abscesses form, then cut it as it should be; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize them until the pus is dried out and all the rotten flesh is removed, then apply ice or cold water and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the ears open and moisture comes to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not drain as it should, know that there is rotten flesh in the bone above, so the instruments do not work: therefore you must tie a piece of linen thread, about a finger thick, and twist it between your fingers into a rope, with a space of a finger or less between each twist; and place the end of the thread in the ear to the patient's ability, and draw it through the odorant until it comes out through the mouth; and many children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for whoever wants to do it; then hold the end that comes out through the nose in one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth in the other hand, and move them up and down alternately as you are sucking on the thread. Do this until you know that the thread has drawn out the rotten flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and reinsert it into the ear as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all the remaining flesh; and then put a plug of cotton in the ear for several days until it is healed, and if there is a need for dry medicines, use them. This is the instrument used to cleanse the head, through which oils and medicines are dropped into the ear.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or bronze, shaped like an open lamp, similar to a candle, and with a handle; and if you want, make a closed vessel, and fill the instrument to cleanse the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart above the chest
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called «telul» arises at the top of the head; it grows and becomes large, so that it is visible to the eye. Therefore, you should treat it at the beginning, and remove all the pus; then place the cautery or burning medicine on it. If one delays covering it until it has become large, then take care whether it is hard, a bad color, or insensible: do not touch it with iron, for it is an abscess, and when one opens it, great harm comes to the patient. But if the abscess is from a superficial touch, and not from a deep color, and you see that one can cover it all, then open the patient and treat the area of dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the head is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when the solution of continuation comes in one of these cartilage work-outs, it profits little, except in some men. Therefore, when this happens to someone, look whether the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the .ij. lips to a stitch, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are torn on both sides, then you should scrape all the parts of their skin until they heal, then assemble the .ij. lips to a stitch, and tighten them, and powder with dragon's blood powder, and burned incense; and put a piece of strong plaster or other binding plaster over the powders, and leave it until it comes off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or with thread, as I have made you aware.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home on the lips there are hard abscesses, similar to grains of wheat, both smaller and larger; therefore you should twist the lips, and cut them with a knife on each nodule, and then take them with tweezers and scrape the area after making an incision with ground vitriol, until the blood is stopped; then use vinegar water, and treat the area with dry substances until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of gum swelling
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth appears on the gums, which the ancients call 'albus'. You should hold it with tweezers, cut it at its root, and let the blood or pus flow; then place powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders, on the spot. If the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; if it does not return after cauterization, that is the way to treat it.
des sordens	of the ears, nose, and throat
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	sometimes they are attached to the roots of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, and there are ugly and rough growths; and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or green, because corruption has reached the gum, and the teeth smell bad; so you should make the patient hold his head in his hands, and press his lips against your finger, and then pull out the teeth or the growths, as far as they will go; and in this way, you should also deal with blackness, yellowness, greenness, and other discoloration, until they are cleaned; and if what is pulled out at first comes back, do it again the next day and the third day, until everything is removed; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments to pull them out, according to what the work shows you, so that the forceps used to extract teeth have different forms from those used between the teeth; and these forms, together with others, should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you are curing a toothache, it is necessary to wait as long as possible before pulling the tooth, because there is no need to hurry. It is a very delicate matter, and one must not be in a hurry to pull it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore, when the patient is compelled to draw breath, you must be certain about the tooth that hurts. Often, the pain deceives the patient and makes them believe it is in the healthy tooth, and they have the good tooth pulled; and yet the pain does not go away because of this as long as the evil tooth remains, for we have already tried this with these patients. And when you are quite certain about the tooth that hurts, you must scrape around the tooth all the way to the gum; then move it with your fingers or with a pair of fine tweezers until it is well loosened, then hold the tweezers tightly in place. Let the head of the patient be between your knees and held firm so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	Then pull out the tooth carefully without breaking it, and if it won't come out, take one of these instruments and insert it into each side lightly, then move it as you did before. And if the tooth is pierced and rotten, you must fill the holes with cotton, where the rottenness is; then hold it tightly with tweezers so that it does not break when pulled; and you must work gently around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part of it behind, which often causes greater pain for the patient due to the root remaining. And beware of doing as ignorant healers do, who, in their haste and arrogance, sometimes break the jaw, without heeding what we have told them; they sometimes bring about serious illness through the holes left by the roots, or by breaking the jaw, as we have often seen. After pulling out the tooth, wash the socket with wine or garlic and salt; and if there is bleeding, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the site; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of instruments, by which the teeth are pulled out first, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not break when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of thick material so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made iron, and they should be toothed to hold the gums.
de la racine des dens	from the root of teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains while pulling, you should put wet cotton on the area for one or two days, until the gums are softened. Then, use tweezers called "algefri", which make the shoulder look like a bird's beak; they should be made inside like a file, and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, then you must uncover the skin all around the root and insert the instrument called "althali", which is a spatula, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root pops out with this, that is good; if not, then use all of the instruments, whose shapes come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one uses this instrument which has .ij. tongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in the reason of teeth, and of this instrument which looks like large tweezers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be sturdy enough that it does not break, and know that many dental instruments exist; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise master subtlety finds his own instrument according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are many diseases for which the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity. And if it does not break in the bone or in other bones, but protrudes, then he seeks the instruments that he needs, that I have told you, and helps with gestures; here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and strong enough to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines, and if there is a protrusion in the bone, and it is small, then treat it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural order of the body, and its shape is unattractive, especially in virginal women, then you should know whether the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down; then pull it out; and if it is airy with the tooth, then take this instrument, of which here is the form, and is similar to a small beak, and let it be made of iron sharpened at the end:
