Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the gum recedes a little every day because of the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that one can be filed, then file it with a file like this is the shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the file that needles are made with; and file the tooth a little every day slightly, so that it does not move until it fits; then smooth it at the end with any rasor, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file the roughness so that it is even and does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth loosen, either by a blow or by falling, and the patient cannot bite down on anything he eats without them coming loose, and you have treated them with binding medicines without success; then they must be restrained with a gold wire, for silver wires turn green and rust, but gold never moves. The wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth. If you wish to direct the teeth, take the wire and wrap it twice between two healthy teeth, then put the wire between the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the bleeding part; then start again at the point where you began, straining your hand gently so that it does not move. Then cut the wire with pliers and assemble the ends, and tie them between the healthy tooth and the loose tooth so that it does not cut the tongue. Then leave it as tightly as possible, and if it comes undone or the wire breaks, then tighten it with another wire. It will stay in place and serve its purpose, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the directing of two healthy teeth and two loose teeth, as you can see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is placed back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and experienced should meddle with this, and sometimes the shape of a tooth from a cow's bone is made, and it is put in the place where there is a defect, and it is held fast as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the line of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this line comes from under the tongue, either by nature from birth or by accident from a wound; and the treatment is to open the mouth of the patient, and place his head in your lap, and loosen the tongue; then cover the nervous line from the side, so that the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is hardness or a knot, and it is caused by a wound, insert the nail and cover the line on the side; and be careful that the split is not too deep, because of the artery that lies underneath. And when you have finished, wet the area with rose water or cold water, then place a tent made of linen under the tongue; and tie the patient's mouth every night so that it does not heal. And if bleeding occurs, apply crushed vitriol; and if the blood stops, cauterize with a lentigo cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat the wound with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre. And if it is inclining towards blenorrhea, and there is moisture, insert the nail, and open it with a subtle spatumile, and release it from one side and the other; and if the bleeding occurs while you are doing this, apply crushed vitriol until it stops, then return to your treatment until you draw out everything. Then wet the area with rose water and celery water, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	There are sometimes growths in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called tonsils. When you treat them as described in the previous section and they do not heal, be aware: if the abscess is firm and small, with a dark color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and has a thick root, do not touch it with iron to prevent bleeding; let it bleed until it is dry, then you can pierce it or it will burst on its own. If it is white in color and the root is thin, prepare an instrument for piercing, but first check that the abscess is calm and soothed. Then have the patient sit facing the sun, with his head tilted back, his mouth open, and his tongue pressed down by a servant holding his hands between the patient's jaws; this will expose the tonsil, which resembles a small knife made of silver or brass:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Having pressed the tongue down with this instrument, you will see the tonsil. Take a pair of forceps and grab the abscess, then pull it out from the tonsil, drawing any threads of membrane along with it. Then cover the instrument again to maintain its shape, for it is designed like a hook; the tip curves upward and the ends curve downward, and they are very sharp. It is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, you can use a pair of tweezers that are shaped like it.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it is sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, then cut the other in the same way, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and water and garlic, and if there is bleeding, then gargle the patient with water, or scoops of pomegranates that have been cooked, or bay leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two tonsils arise in the throat, so cut them then as you did the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was deep in her throat, that is to say, one small abscess; and she had almost closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the opening which was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for one or two more days. And the abscess had risen so high that it had pushed out two bumps from the two openings of the nose. I hurried therefore, and inserted an instrument into one opening, then drew out a large amount of pus; then I made another incision in the other opening of the nose, and cleared her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards, I inserted the instrument into the abscess, and cut out a portion, and only a little blood came out; and thus the opening of the throat of the woman was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut the abscess for a long time; and it would grow again and fill up the space that I had emptied, so that it became very large; therefore, I lanced it and cauterized it inside her throat; thus, it did not grow any more. And I left these parts, and she was to continue the treatment herself.
de l’uve	of the liver
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the eye descends to the socket and is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round, it is called an "eye". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the wound of the aperture is soothed, and it is thin; and it is round and not long; and it is blood-red, or light brown, or black, then you should avoid cutting into it. For there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it according to the manner I have described, in its whiteness and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, pull it downward, and cut to a depth of one-third or half the length of the two instruments I mentioned for cutting into the two almonds. You should not cut deeper than the natural limit, for if you do, it causes grief in speech and voice. After the incision, use what we said about the incision on the two almonds, and continue the treatment until it is healed. And if the patient fears having their eye cut, then you should use an agent to numb the sensation of pain before cauterizing. The method of cauterization is as follows: the patient places his head on your lap, and you press his tongue against the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, and apply quicksilver, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; then use the implement made for this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a handle at the top where the medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon; and you place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye, and the patient lies on his side so that the saliva and mucus from the medicine do not run down into the throat and lungs; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it harden and the burning sensation of the medicine subside. Then take some cotton, wrap it around an instrument, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and insert the instrument wrapped in cotton into the canal above, so that the cotton rests on the eye; do this frequently until the cautery is complete, then let it dry for four or five days. If you need to apply the cautery again, do so, then wash the area around the medicine with cool water, and treat the wound with gargarisms until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or cautery. If it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take calamus, hyssop, marjoram, rue, chamomile, wormwood, and similar herbs, and mix some of them in a pot with honey, and boil it; the pot should be well-glazed with strong clay, and inside the pot there is an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it can be made of silver or bronze, and one of the eyes is placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the cane, until the eye is mortified; afterwards, he begins again frequently, until the eye dries up, and take care that you do not do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many things happen there; and do not do it except at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put inside it an egg-shell, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the egg-shell does not allow the vapor to weigh down the mouth, and it is a good and safe remedy together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a fish bone or spine, or some other thing, gets stuck in the throat; so you must draw out what you can see and press the tongue against the sun with all your strength, so that you can move the object; and if it does not become apparent to you and remains stuck in the throat, you should make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting. Or the patient may swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches its place, it will catch on, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out in the way we have said, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be bent at the tip so that it can more easily enter the throat, and its tip should be lifted up; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, or it will fold over, nor push the os inside; and move it around so that the patient swallows the instrument, in order that it can dislodge the object; then he swallows it down, or you pull it out with the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the mucus of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the mucus is treated with medicine as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look in the throat of the patient at the sun, and then press his tongue with the instrument that I told you. And if you see the mucus, then pull it out with a small hook, or with tiny tweezers suitable for this. And if this doesn't work, take a sheep's horn, and put it in the throat of the patient, then heat the tip of the horn, and do this often. And if the patient turns pale all day, then take a full glass of cold water, open his mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it around with his hand often; and as soon as the mucus feels the water, it will shrink.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not shrink as we have said, then suffocate the patient with assafetida, using the instrument that I described for the fumigation of the larynx; do this many times, because it will certainly work. And the method of the fumigation is to put burning coals in a pot, and cover it with a perforated lid, and place the instrument in the hole; then blow your fumigation into the pot, and have the patient put the tip of the horn in his mouth, and close his mouth so that no smoke escapes, but reaches the mucus; and the mucus will shrink immediately. And if it does not shrink, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient fast, and eat salty and dry things, and drink no water; and then he will certainly pass it.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to pull out the mucus is, when you can see it, like curved tweezers that can enter the throat; and it has the shape of a bird's beak, and is coated with limestone, so that what it grabs cannot escape; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many kinds of abscesses, as the recollections which come to us here and there in this book show, and they differ in penetration and size; and there are two main types, one depending on its appearance, and the other on its location in the body. Thus, an abscess in the head is different from one in the fundament, and a soft-tissue abscess is different from one which occurs in a joint, and each type must be treated differently.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And one must not lance an abscess until the boil is mature according to its nature; and there are some which one must lance when they are crusty, and do not heal by themselves according to their nature, like abscesses which come in joints. For when an abscess comes in a joint, and you leave it as long as it is purulent around the edge, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint will be damaged, causing contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess is near the principal limb, and you delay lancing it until it is mature, it will harm the principal limb; but if it is near the fundament, one should lance it so that it matures; and one must not lance a crusty abscess without digestion being complete, except for one which is near the fundament, lest it become impacted within and grow longer, and a fistula develops; and it will not heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And one must know the time for lancing an abscess which is mature according to its nature, and that is when the pain has subsided, and there is a reduction in fever, and lessening of pain and redness, and relaxation and softening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and one should lance it where it is most dependant, and where there is an opening for pus to escape; and the lancing should be done from the long side of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints affecting nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In these cases, treat according to the affected member. And when an abscess is in a fleshy location, it is better to leave it intact until digestion is complete, as we have said. For if you pierce it before that, the body from which the venom comes will be elongated, and it will be filled with much filth; and the lips and depths of it may harden. And for some abscesses, one should cut according to the width of the body, according to what the member requires. One should treat small abscesses with small openings, and large abscesses with large openings, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess. For some abscesses, one should slice off the top and cover it; when it has become like a drape, and is deadened, one should do as one does with blisters. Some are split into three angles, and some are covered like the leaf of a myrtle, like abscesses of the joints. And for some, one makes a round incision, and other incisions, and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those without a head, such as a superficial abscess, should be pierced directly. And when an abscess is large and has drawn a lot of pus, if you do not draw out all the pus in one hour, but some in one day, then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more; do this repeatedly from great to small, until all the pus comes out. The same is true if the patient is very weak, or a woman carrying a child, or a small child, or an elderly person. For sometimes the pus shoots out with such force that it may kill the patient, and you would not know it. Therefore, be very cautious with this chapter; when you have pierced your abscess, wash the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; if it is a plain incision, treat it with tents made of linen or old cotton. If it is a large abscess with many openings, put a tent into each one so that they touch each other. If you have sliced off part of the skin and cut around it, fill it with old cotton or raw linen cloth without moisture, and leave it for three days; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, treat it with cold water and ash, and wet a cloth, and place it over the bleeding area repeatedly. And if the bleeding persists, administer treatment and care, and the powders that I have described earlier in this book; and if it is winter, and the location of the abscess is very nervous, then place wet tents and cloths moistened with warm wine and oil over it; and if it is summer, and the location is fleshy, then place wet cloths moistened with water and oil, or with cold wine and oil, for three days, as we have said. Then dislodge the abscess, wash and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.Et se il adonques ne percoit point li pus, et il est gros et froit, si covient que tu traies la bowe derechief tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie; et li digeresce les sances, et l’essue sus l’eschape; puis le cure d’oignement ou d’aisil et de viez oile dou frotier, si com il covient.  Et se il adonques percoit point li pus, et il est gros et chaud, si covient que tu traies derechief la bowe en digestion acomplie, et li digeresce les sances, et l’essue sus l’eschape; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se il adonques percoit point li pus, et il est petit et froit, si covient que tu traies derechief la bowe en digestion acomplie; et li digeresce les sances, et l’essue sus l’eschape; puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et se il adonques percoit point li pus, et il est petit et chaud, si covient que tu traies derechief la bowe en digestion acomplie; et li digeresce les sances, et l’essue sus l’eschape; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And now we must discuss generally about treating abscesses: I have already told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and now see the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Now let's talk about how to treat abscesses that come from the head; they are similar to those found on chickens, and there are many variations. Some are fatty and have a soft texture like poultry, while others are hard and stony, and there is no cause for concern if the artery doesn't react. The treatment for these varies depending on the individual case. You must use an instrument called an "entromissoire" to examine the content of the abscess; if it contains moisture, you should lance it from the side; otherwise, if it's stony, you should cut it out. After removing the moisture, you should scorch the skin to prevent any remaining moisture from coming back; it will return if you don't do this. Then, apply cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, or water and salt if the ointment is unavailable, and leave it overnight. The next day, reapply the cotton, and continue doing this until the wound is healed. If the abscess contains a fatty nodule, lance it from the side; squeeze it from all sides and remove the entire core; if the artery reacts, follow the instructions I gave earlier. Treat the wound with ointment suitable for healing.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	The incision on a stony abscess is easier if there is less blood. In some cases, I found abscesses on the heads of elderly women that were like hard, rough, white stones, and couldn't be broken; if one tried to pierce them, it would have caused as much damage as a stone. The openings for these types of abscesses should be made as low as possible so that the pus can drain out; then treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times this abscess occurs in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere in the body, and they are numerous, and some are joined together. Each scrofula is properly located within its coat, just as the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similarities among these scrofulae. There are some which contain moisture, and others that refuse to yield to treatment. If you see one in a good condition for cauterization, and it resembles the color of the body, and is flat on each side and not raised towards the nerves of the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not deep; then you should cover it from above, and cut into each part, and the two lips of the heart are joined together, if you need to, as we have said in the case of abscesses of the head; and draw it out little by little, and be sure that you do not cut into the nerve or the vein, and do not allow the spatula to slip and cut, so that the hand does not escape, and do not go too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut into the vein and it does not allow you to work, then put vitriol powder or other powders that stop bleeding into the wound, and tie it up; and leave it until the abscess is calmed down and the wound softens and begins to suppurate. And when the blood has clotted, return to your work, until you finish it; then seek out any small scrofulae that remain, and cut and clean them. And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, then you should not cut into that scrofula at its root, but ligate it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by it without harm; then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut away the whole scrofula, then you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now so that there is no superfluity remaining due to the size of the scrofula. Then you must attend to covering its root, pulling it outward, and sewing it as we have said. For those scrofulas which hold a superfluity, pierce where it appears dead; and pierce in the same way as that previously described, hanging a tent with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is clean, treat it with an ointment enfolding charcoal until it heals.
de squinance	of squint.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients wrote and spoke of throat-slitting; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the script of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, it is necessary that the flap of the throat, which is called the "epiglottis", be cut; and one should not make an incision through this, because all the veins and the lung of the patient are in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent loss of life due to strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we should split it below three or four circles, or a small split across the middle, between two circles, or according to the amount of the split in the larynx; not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these places are suitable for the split of the epiglottis, that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, then he should stretch the skin of the throat to the very edge, then split the larynx until it reaches the windpipe; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cover the larynx, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and is demonstrated by the section of the vein of the finger that jumps out through the place that is broken, and by the failure of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leaves the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one fears strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the neck, and stitch it up all the way to the cartilage without leaving a gap; then administer remedies that promote healing until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely swollen and the patient is judged to be at death's door and the shortage of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, grasp the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease was passed, and it is passed in 3 or 4 days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And therefore they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, as soon as it was cured;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young girl take a knife and thrust it into her throat, cutting some of the vocal cords in her larynx;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that the blood which had issued from it had not flowed out any further than the throat, and the blood vessels were intact.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, sewed up the wound, and healed her so that she recovered.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and had not the lady fainted from the pain, and returned after to her senses;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in the color of yellow, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it has two causes: natural and accidental; where nature has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is in two ways: one similar to a tumor, and the other way is like an abscess that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear in it, and one should not operate with force except on the small one, and test and examine throughout the entire opening.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it as a tumor, and it cannot be moved at all, cut it like one cuts a tumor, and treat it throughout its growth, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and seek treatment immediately, and heal it as it should be, until it is completely healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of us, all of which I will describe:
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now I must tell you about the difference between a wound and an outbreak.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that a discharge is a persistent fever and heat until the boil has burst and completed its course; then the fever and heat will cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a boil there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a pustule, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a pimple, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are according to their appearances, some are greasy, some moist, and their colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of a boil, you must first test and examine it with an instrument called a "probes", according to what its shape indicates in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses in the brain is to press on the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and gradually turn your fingers, until you know that the instrument has pierced through to the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then withdraw the instrument, and take care that nothing leaks out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the pus runs clear, whatever its colour, they should proceed as I have said for other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if no pus comes out after the instrument is inserted, know that it is a dry abscess, so they should cross it with the instrument and take it with tweezers, and lightly scorch each part, and guard the coat or shirt that the patient wears to make sure it is clean.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out intact, then draw it out piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return to the body many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if some remains and the wound does not trouble you, then treat the wound with some corrosive powders, and bind the wound tightly, and apply hot poultices to soothe the abscess, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with that which causes pus.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is pulsating, or any other vein that you are hastening, use vitriol and leave it for 2 or 3 days until the wound suppurates and the bleeding stops; then return to the cupping as before.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the cutting instruments, and they are in 3 ways: large, medium, and small; and there are 4 squares that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are 3 kinds of ways to use them: large, medium, and small, to surround abscesses with fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	They are also like the needles that they use to sew sorcerers, and they are made of brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are better than those that are blackened with lead for surrounding abscesses with fistulas.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	They are in 3 ways: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of warts are very varied, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and some warts have two curves in three ways.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and some warts have three curves and are also in three ways; and some warts have two curves and are only in one way, and some warts have one curve and are in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The tips of these which are used for cutting are sharp, and there are some that do not cut except on one side, so that they do not cut the vein or nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and these introducers are wrapped in pieces of cloth so that the patient does not hurt themselves when opening abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are of three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and we do not use them except in fleshy places, such as legs and arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes another small instrument is made, similar to a piece of wood, according to this form, with which blood is staunched:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes put in the place that heals by copious bleeding of the veins and arteries, and sometimes they are made according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	At times, men's breasts swell when they become corrupt, so much so that they look like women's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	They remain ugly and swollen; anyone who wants to treat them should follow this method from line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scorch the fat, and fill the wound with a poultice of warm honey, then stitch together the two lips of the wound, and let it heal;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast sags and becomes soft due to its size, as it does in women, then split it into two along a similar line;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	with the larger line containing the smaller according to this form, from this line b to line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cut the skin between the two lips and remove the fat, and use what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for treatment, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely closed because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with wet cotton dipped in corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it absorbs the remainder and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpit
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpit are like hard scrofula nodules, some of which contain pus and moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been discharged, then fill the wound with clean cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofula, they should be treated as we have said for fissures of scrofula, and if the wound is deep, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of bleeding from an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sewn shut, there often occur abscesses and swelling of the vein;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows it is caused by the artery, then the abscess will be long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you will sense a pull; and when it is in the vein, there will be a visible pulsation;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is below the armpits and in the groin and neck and many other places, and it is large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one should avoid the cure with iron, and if it is on the head, one should also avoid it, and in the one who has swelling of an artery, they should cut through the skin from above.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then open the incision with knives, and carefully cut the artery away from the veins, until it is fully exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	take a needle and insert it under the eye, piercing all the way to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread about half an inch, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then probe the area between the two ligatures with an introducer until blood emerges and the abscess is relieved;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the treatment that causes bleeding, until the ligature falls off;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is by the size of the vein, then you must hold in your hand as much of the abscess as you can to all the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the area that you are holding in your hand, and pierce it, and thread .i. double thread through it, so that you can pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I have told you, to one of the two parts with the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will come undone, then tie another needle to all of the thread under the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads in .iiij. directions;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then lance the abscess so that the pus flows out, then lance the pus from the chest and leave what is attached.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then treat the wound with poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As well as abscesses coming in the artery and vein, they come to the nerves when they are injured, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens most often in shoulders and elbows and all joints where there are articulations, and it is a deep abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in various states without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body, but under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it is motionless in all parts, and does not go forward or backward, or sideways or upward, and that which is in joints should not be covered with iron; for there might be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And that which is on the head or forehead, treat with a plaster.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and squeeze at its base;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, then open it with an incision and scrape away at the flesh, then pull out the bone and stitch up the wound until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes they occur in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called 'fungus' due to its resemblance to ears, with fine hair and large lumps; there are both small and very large ones;
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	I saw one man who had two on his stomach that looked more like mushrooms than anything else; there was no difference between them, they were white with thin roots and split open, and moisture flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found one weighing eighteen ounces and the other six ounces; their appearance in the incision is such that you should examine whether the patient is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist with a thin root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	If the cut is large, and the patient has a strong pulse, then you must act quickly with the fire cautery, because when cutting there is often excessive bleeding that cannot be stopped until cauterized.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision by the knife, then take a well-prepared thread, tie off the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not stop squeezing the hair Follicle until it pops out of the joint, and squeeze through it without effort; and if the roots are thick, it is afraid to pop them out because of the belly, but you can certainly squeeze out half of them.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and be careful not to squeeze the follicle that is of a pale color and poor sensation and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of cancer later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil pops
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the hernia comes from cauterization of a wound or fissure in syphilis, and it is on the abdomen and some of the bowels, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is mentioned earlier, or from flatulence;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is from the rupture of syphilis and from the exit of the bowels, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a slight thing without pain, and it opens with various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with their fingers, it rises, and then returns, and sometimes it is serous, and increases a lot at the entrance of the bath and with great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a slight thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, nor does it constrict at all; and if it is due to blood, then it opens through these signs of large and hard abscesses, and it is fixed according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to flatulence, then it is relieved by the touch, and the operations are such that you should look to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	You should let it heal. For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the bladder, then you should instruct the patient to tighten his abdomen and extend it straight, then sign all around the navel;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to sit up quickly between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the area you have marked all around the joint.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then cut through the top half of the abscess to the bottom at the large hook;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it tightly with a strong thread, or strong silk cord, and have the patient hold onto it firmly;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then cut through the top half of the abscess extended over the string, and push your index finger in, and grasp the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught in the lining, free it and push the intestine back into the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find an obstruction, they cut it at the obstacle and cut away the excess;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery or vein causes a blockage, then go around it and return to your work and take two needles, thread them with two strong threads, and pierce the two needles through what you have done in a cross shape.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then squeeze the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you see any pus, remove the needles and let it drain until it is clean, and cut away the dead flesh.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	where you cut it when it is subtle and delicate, then treat it as appropriate, and lance the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area as appropriate and close it up.
dou chancre	from a ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the types of ulcers and how to treat them with medicine, as well as the importance of cauterization with iron. Now, let us speak of the ulceration that occurs in the mouth, and the great caution that must be taken in its treatment. The ancients said that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be reached, such as in the breast or armpit, and in similar places, it should all be removed when it is in its early stages. However, once it becomes large and old, one must not touch it, for I have never seen anyone heal from this.
