et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these four together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then re-insert the needle into the part where you began, in the manner of sewing cloth.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and make the distance between each stitch the thickness of a thumb nail;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch should be seven times the length of the needle;
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed a wound that a man had on his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which had been made by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm in length,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines protruded well over two palms in length,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was on his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I returned the intestine to him after it had been outside his body for twenty-four hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	The wound was sewn up and healed within fifteen days, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And those who saw him believed that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I didn't treat it with ointments because I was in a place where there were none to be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you about two proper methods of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and tie it to the end of a thread;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the right heart directly, then insert the needle into the throat or cost where you have blown.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and pierce through from the other side of the part inside just to the skin;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as the leather workers do skins,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leave one side of the throat once and grab it from the other, so that the stitch is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, which Galen describes properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is if it is like how two parts are naturally joined together.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	They apply one end of the thread to one end, in such a way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	take a needle and pierce only that spot nearby,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let the two jaws of the forceps
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and pierce from the outside to the inside,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as two jaws of the forceps;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce one and the other from the outside to the inside, in two other jaws of the forceps that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the usual method of sewing, and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen says this, and some people testify to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one should sew the belly with two needles, having thread on each;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is in the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	the incision is more difficult than in other places in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, so that the fire has moved it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if one re-inserts the intestines and sews up the wound; then put on the cauterizing powder mixed with charcoal,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if it burns the meat, put some ointment on it that is at hand until the wound heals over;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and tie the thread tightly and sew up the slits, and the mawmet and the apes;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with the others until it is healed;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicine, apply aged cotton
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For in many simple wounds, you need no other medicine;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will spread to the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	if it is necessary to moisten with a light woolen cloth dipped in warm oil, or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the joints, and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if there is pain or swelling in the bones, and this happens many times,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	treat him with warm rose oil, or olive oil,
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierces inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine which is called 'young' cannot heal when it is raw,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is because of the thinness of the veins that they are, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the thread is cut from the wound, he puts it back as soon as possible while the intestine is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	if it is old and turned red or black, then you should ligature the area that is black so that no blood flow comes from it,
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries in it;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligature,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put both shoulders hanging from the part below the wound until relieved for extraction when the stitches are removed, and the wound is closed.
de la routure dou boueil	of the treatment of boils
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are damaged, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	one can repair it in some ways,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw a man pierce his belly with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and was the wound on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it was filled and became a fistula, and from it came the digestion and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to apply poultices until it was healed and the wounds closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw that it had healed, I feared that the patient still had evil in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and it did not harm him, but he remained in good health, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimentalists say that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it must be bound in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take lamb's testicles, then bring together the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the scrotum has opened, put it on both lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if he opens his mouth upward;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then he strikes him on the head, and it remains so that he cannot release himself,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another tremor after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely seized;
et cout la plaie.	and watch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If they get stuck in the intestines and cause no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	one can tie the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the tip of this intestinal thread and make sure it is very dry,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread a thin, twisted flax thread
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then thread the needle with the flax thread and sew up the wound; and then dislocate it again in the same place.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of sewing up a hernia is not successful except according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no healing except by subtle means.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and especially when it is deep and narrow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the green knotting of a hard and white node, where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is like a feather on an bird's wing;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it is clear and translucent, and other times opaque;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and other times large enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	And I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not healed and has no scabs;
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	this occurs only for one of the eight reasons;
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is, by the littleness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh within it, and upon the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where there is too much bowing;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	the bones are porous, and the tissue is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not effective in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a type of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the nature of the region, digestion is slow, and health comes late, and it swells by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already demonstrated all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must tell you about the treatment of a fistula that is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the sinus, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in any of the sides,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it affects the principal organ, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all of these fistulas that are in this way are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	And if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have described, and you trust its treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see it, take a tent of copper or iron, if the fistula is straight, so take it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is crooked, then search for a slender, blunt needle
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the slender one bends around the crook;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot probe it well with needles,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you cleanse it through one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for moisture quickly passes from one hole to another and cleanses.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you should let it bleed until you can tell whether there is bone or nerve, and it is completely healed.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know for sure the location, whether it is near a joint, nerve, artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the ways I have told you, if the cup according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the foulness and putrefied matter within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat the wound until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is deep in a straight line, you must open it as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I wet the tent with medicine water, and insert it to the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I apply heating ointments to healthy flesh, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve causes you distress in your limbs, as we have said,
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is rot and darkness within it, then cut into it until all the rot is removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cleanse it with healing things until it is healed,
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed, return to the previous steps as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not yet reached the spring:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you uncover and desire to reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if this is so, then it is healthy.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other way except to let nature take its course;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone that is corrupted, and you can pull it out with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if he pulls with .a. suitable instrument for this,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, he should pull them all out;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes it difficult, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then grip and hold firm, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put something on the wound to encourage pus.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it fester around the bone,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have looser bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you simply treat the corruption until the darkness is completely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great deal of corruption and it reaches to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it needs to be cut away and covered all the way to the corruption, then clean the wound until it is healed over;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula which happened to a man on his leg.
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the matters came to the leg, and was swollen with a large abscess, and had no cause to discharge in order to open;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but their madness made them work so much that they opened the abscesses
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and much matter came out and became a fistula, and many openings appeared from which pus and moisture flowed from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many received treatment for two years, and there was no wise man in medicine
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was called to see him, and saw his leg and the medicines used to treat him,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what runs through the openings of the body to a great extent;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the bodies of young men became red and had a citron-like colour.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I pitched a tent at one of these openings, and then I explored all the openings,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that they connected with each other throughout the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened therefore, and struck one of the holes, so that I uncovered a part of the bone;
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and pierced through, and the corruption reached up to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and believed that there was no other corruption except for that which I took out;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to heal the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but it would not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then recommenced, and exposed the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and removed it, and then took care to close up the site;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not, although I cut around a palm of the bone, and let it drop out completely,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	and then restored it with medicine; and it healed quickly and closed up,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there is no need to repeat the procedure except for the weakness of the patient who cannot endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and the fear of death I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For there was often bloodletting but he was completely healed
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and grew on the bone a hard lump, and he was in good condition and did not have any discomfort or contrary effect in all places, neither in eating nor moving around.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken anywhere in the body, then it must be treated in this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take a string, and tie it around the head of the bone that is exposed,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct someone to pull it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another thicker string made of wool over the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and are drawn up, so that you treat the corrupted flesh underneath,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the site where you see swelling, so that the swelling does not break the skin;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a hot brand or a flat object underneath the bone to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and one must draw out as much of the swelling as one can see and feel, and draw it out again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is broken, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	and discovers all the flesh; then put a hot iron underneath
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then sew from one side of the corruption to the other, and let the sewing be as far from the corruption as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut through the corrupted joint, and sew up the bone on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the dislocation is in the two joints, there is no other cure except to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the dislocation is at the knuckle of the hand or the ankle, it is a very serious matter,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless you must investigate the dislocation, how it appeared to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way you can, but be careful not to hurt the vein or nerve;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and you will know that the tools and needles for cutting these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of the ears.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and their thinness, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason one must prepare for each type of work its instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and you will know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the manners of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	then prepare the instrument you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	Shoulders can dislocate due to internal causes or external causes;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated this corrosion with remedies, but they are ineffective,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then cover the affected limb up to the site of the corrosion,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes either by death or, more likely, by the defect in the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb becomes black and appears burnt by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then after darkness comes, then goes that corrosion of limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes over the whole body; so you should hurry to cover it,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it's from the sting of some venomous beasts, like a scorpion, viper, and similar creatures,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is on the head or face, then cover it, and do not give it any space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes just to the hand, then grip at the joint so that the cautery does not come up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then grip at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no use in remedies that do not match its potency;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And do the same when the cautery comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then grip after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, cut off the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends into the leg, cut off at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to cut off the patient's leg;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of binding the member whether above or below is that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and one assistant stretches one of the ligaments down, and another assistant stretches the other ligament up,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you loosen the flesh which is between the two ligaments by one spatulum wide, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or tie off the thread, and place a linen pad on each side so that the thread does not touch the healthy tissue,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring about another injury and abscess in the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if there is bleeding when you operate, cauterize the wound heavily.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	Or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then bind the injured member with suitable bandages and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to a certain man in his sleep:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he experienced darkness resembling a burn from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corrosion began in his toe of the foot, until it spread all over the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered the foot and it healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and a long time after, the corrosion returned in his finger of the hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I placed things that cause reverberation after cleansing the body, but he could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cup his hand, but I refused because I had no hope of reverberating the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut his hand, he would die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the strength of the man was weak; and he gave up hope altogether and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he put a bandage on his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	I have told you everything for now, in case someone else needs to know more.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy part, and remains so long that it causes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they burst and discharge, and the place remains hollow, just like vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin above is as delicate as a loose napkin
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not extend to the bone or nerve, and such an injury is called "superficial".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called a "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it extends to the bone, it is called a  "fistula".;
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and cure it by covering all around with a cloth, especially when it is thin like a kerchief.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not fear its destruction.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you are confident that the skin will heal and there is no deep corruption,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Examine if the breasts are swollen, and if the nipples have a foul odor.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then cleanse them with an Egyptian medicine made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take asafotida, oil, and litharge, in equal parts, and mix them together while heating in a vessel over fire,

et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and they use it as an enema for the breast, and constrict the orifice;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for about two hours, then remove it by squeezing it out;

et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, or the Egyptian medicine or the water from ashes,

Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Because when the bow is fully drawn, no arrow should be loosed.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish,

car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the bow is fully drawn, no arrow should be loosed.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish,

pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply a soft ointment on another piece of cloth according to the size of the opening,

et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And the one who is on the breast's opening, remove often to remove the pain,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what flows from the bowels, whether it is venom, or pus, or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has extended in such a way, and you see the nature that rises through the aperture of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast milk has dried up, and approaches health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loosen it in the morning, or noon, and when you loosen the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	change another cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows for many days, know that the breast will not dry up.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons persist after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because saints are near. For there are men who slowly heal wounds with ointments, and others who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if food is indigestible and a woman vomits after many days, know that her milk will not dry up;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts are slow to dry up, and are distant, then apply medicines which are moist in substance but dry in effect;
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as diaphenon ointment, for it contains a large portion of vitriol, and that is the best medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take a definite ointment, and make it with rose oil, and rose wine of equal substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and with the same, you can make cooked honey thickening,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when a definite ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them into powder over the honey while it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then they glue a piece of cloth, and apply it to the chest, and sometimes they administer a long aristolache.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestial lily, which is like flour of wheat and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simples or compounds: grind them into powder, and put it on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is long, and is not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then you know that the corruption is complete, and it makes an impression on the bone, or in the hard parts of the body, or in the soft tissues.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if there is a wound from a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panaritys is an abscess that arises under the fingernail of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or from the foot, or perhaps it grows in other parts;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and not treated, an abscess will form;
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they grow and flow pus as far as the root of the nail, and perhaps further;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion goes to the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the toe becomes swollen, and its colour turns yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	you should cut away all the excess growth under the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses against the flesh, and begins to grow out, and bleeds,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you must put the thread under the nail so that it does not pierce the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and pull it upwards gently and slowly,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put medicine on the remaining flesh to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the pimples until they heal.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and draw it out, because as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the tooth腐, cut it out in one of the gums as previously described,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it heals;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wild, and biting, and it feels great pain, then you must heal it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail of the little finger slantingly from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	You should treat the hemorrhoids that grow in some people's hands by chance, which are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is bone, and sometimes fingernails,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some grow at the base of the joint where the finger meets the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born with a hernia in his navel must not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And he who is born at the joint of the navel, by chance moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of that which is fleshy if it is light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; you must keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	For one who is born where the anus should be, you must first cut around the flesh circularly down to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut the bone to a suitable depth, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come from birth, or from joining a wound, or from a burn, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	Then you must treat this fracture so that the bones heal according to their natural shape.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	And put between two tents or dampened cloths in rose oil so they do not fuse together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you could place between two thin pieces of wood, until the joints are healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If this swelling comes to either palm with the fingers, then treat this fracture as it should be done.
Des vils	Of evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Wounds are large enveloping openings filled with melancholy superfluities that come from various parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in other people.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer an emetic to him occasionally, and then cleanse him with basil water.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with fire is according to two methods: one is that they cut it, and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you open a vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	Incision is according to this manner: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the large veins are dilated,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch the leg from the ailment above the thigh down to the part under the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then open the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a broad incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then squeeze and draw out the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bandage it, and instruct him to drink possets made with black gall;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and resume the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, as is beneficial for the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The treatments for this are as follows: shave the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in water, and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire, and then cup the vein from above at the knee, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the Achilles tendon, and scorch the vein from both sides, until it appears when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then pierces the vein below, until it is raised from the skin, and then it can be pricked gently,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then scrape the skin above the vein until it bleeds, then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it with the vein, as you did before, and prick it with another needle, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another wound, or several if you need to, then lift it, and cut at the heel of the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull and lift until the second wound; then extract it from wound to wound, until it comes out completely, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull and lift it, then thread a needle with two strong threads,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	then tie it and pull it out, and put it under a thread, then turn your hand from side to side until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be sure it does not pop, for if it pops, one cannot milk or raise it, and the patient will suffer harm.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have finished milking it, place a compress of wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound, and treat it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the wound is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, not straight as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	you must split it tortuously, but do not pop it; and milk it as we have already said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the knife with which one opens the vein is curved, and does not cut unless it opens the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And its handle is thick because if it were slender, it would cut the vein; but it must be thick as we have said, and this is how it should be shaped:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is twisted in legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes they grow elsewhere than on the legs, and this happens from the porridge that comes under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	like serpents and worms that wriggle between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the color changes, and the vein begins to come out, just like a plant root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the wound is open, you must wrap it with a piece of linen from one and a half fingers to two and a half fingers thick, and the knot,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the linen hang loose on the leg, and every time it slips out of place, wrap it around the linen and the knot.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cover the root at all until it has completely healed.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cover it, it will go into the flesh and cause an abscess and pus and illness in that spot.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	that it must be treated slowly until it reaches the head, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein when treated for two or three palmeds long, or ten,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and a man came to me whose vein was ten palms long, and when you cover it, it pierces like a needle and goes all the way through,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and after emptying the matter inside, apply healing medicine to it for several days, then treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein bleeds freely, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot, or on the foot itself,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it flows profusely, and it jumps like a spring; therefore treat it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that grow between skin and flesh:
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "cow disease" in our land because it often affects cows:
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and there is a small worm which is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body, ascending and descending.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it can be felt as it moves from one member to another, until it breaks through the skin where it is going, and jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it causes swelling from certain humours, like worms and snakes and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one fears its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and milked, one cannot help but feel pity when it moos:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	Therefore, you must tie the udder firmly above and below with a strong string,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then milk it from above and pull it hard, and if the milk is mixed with blood in the udder and you do not milk it out,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize it with fire above it as it dies
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, then squeeze under his eyebrow firmly, then pull upwards and out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and one must use a cleansing agent for the body with digestive remedies for putrid humours,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and they are sick from eating poisonous meat.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vomiting" in our language, and it is a pain that occurs in some parts of the body, especially in the chest and abdomen, caused by the movement of wind or air. It can be acute and short-lived or chronic and long-lasting. People may experience symptoms such as belching, flatulence, or regurgitation of food.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from one member to another; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rise up like a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	quicker than anything else, just like quicksilver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that spot and moved to the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little while later, it ran through the whole body until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then he told me that it turned around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very amazed at how she moved from limb to limb like this; for I had never seen this disease progress in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many who experienced pain moving from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not want to, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because women have dry skin and uncovered veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this, the wind is forced out.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And it does not appear in those who are healthy, who have moist skin and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	examine above and below carefully, and then press gently until that forced wind leaves its place;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it with your own eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure for those who draw out winds, as with fetid pills, and pills of serapin, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the parts of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their points is such that there are some with large, small, flat, and twisted points;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some with two angles, and some with tongues, and some with pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and dislocation occurs in any limb in two ways: either in a principal limb it dislocates,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it therefore dislocates in any of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you about later appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must be careful about extracting this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many cases;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not completely out, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of a brain injury when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and the cerebrospinal fluid leaks out from above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is stabbing pain and swelling and redness in the affected area, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and loss of consciousness, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes there is blood coming out of the nose or ears; and sometimes they lose their speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaps from the wound moisture white like pus, and also jumps as if from a burn.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears to you, then hold back on the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the wound when it falls on the heart are that it is close to the left breast, and feels as if it were pierced into a hard object, not soft;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the wound also becomes mute like the pulse, and short black blood comes out, and there is coldness and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	you know without a doubt that death will follow.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that never leaves the lung is foam coming from the mouth, and the throat swollen, and the patient's color changing, and panting heavily and seeking the cool air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces the covering of the foot, it is near the small bones; and it causes great pain and great swelling and panting; and all the limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, by chance some undigested food may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the gut, and no feces escape through the bowels, then there is no hope of a cure, nor in extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, and urine escapes and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and spine of the back and hip and thigh and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him on the jaw, at the root of his teeth:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it, and extracted it from beneath the fat of the ear, and he was healed without a trace.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I extracted an arrow that had struck him in the grease of his eye underneath, underneath the eyelid:
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	The arrow was bent back on itself, and he could not touch it except for the tip towards his face,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And it was a great arrow from a Turkish bow, and it went through his ear; the jugular vein was healthy, and no bad accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he took an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it went through his ear;
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I removed the barb, and pulled gently until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And he took an arrow in his house, which was lodged in his belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then if he has not passed .xxx days, he will not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and extracted it, and had no bad outcome.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man whom an arrow has struck in the back, and the wound is closed over:
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions do not change,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	he finds no harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man who had an arrow wound to the face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and he remained like that without great pain; and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And they extracted an arrow from a noble man of the king's household, who had been struck in the eye,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was a little tilted to the right side; and the arrow was fully drawn out
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the wound after she had been bled for three days. I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I examined her thoroughly and felt nothing amiss;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and she had a pointed pain under her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed an attractive and digestive plaster on the spot because the skin was swollen;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the mark of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the plaster more frequently, and the wound healed quickly, and the patient suffered for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he felt the arrow one day within his flesh; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was opened,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which protruded at the site;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted in the opening of the wound with that medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and transgressed the terms for four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then he lanced the wound that I had punctured with tongs, and probed it from side to side, but could not extract it;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Therefore I did not cease to use subtle and ingenious tools until the following day, when I took well-made tongs,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what his condition will be by the end of this chapter, until I treated and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot heal:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and sewed up the wound, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I will tell you about the extraction of some arrows:
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you can apply your treatment according to what I say and not according to what the books say, for the books cannot encompass everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters consider very little of what is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	and they do not seek out new works or new tools, or the descents of foreign things which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows grow in the members where they are stuck in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumped out from where it entered, is an arrow entering the flesh, and sometimes jumps out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump out now, leave it until the flesh around it has rotted away and the exit wound has healed;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is lodged in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it for several days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump out, and if it doesn't, then pierce around the arrowhead with a thin, sharp tool until the flesh around it is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull, and pierces one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents I have mentioned are apparent to the patient: then do not pull it out, but leave it until it is even with the skin after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow pierces the brain, it is fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is not lodged in the bone and does not pierce the brain,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for some days without mishap, if the device pulls.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very loose and cannot come out, then administer cauteries around it as I have told you, then cleanse the area once it has healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged deep in the body and cannot be seen, then cut her all over to find it.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	there is no bone or nerve or vein, then cut as deeply as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs inside that are holding it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	remove the flesh that is pierced by it up to the depth of 1/7 of a palm as deeply as you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or fold the ears of the arrow so that you can draw it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and skillfully so that you do not break the arrow as you pull it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it in one go, then leave it until the surrounding tissue has swollen; then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding makes you feel contrary, then administer what we have said about curing in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting the nerve and of opening a vein, and use whatever means you can to draw out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and adjust the patient according to the position he was in when the arrow struck.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for that is the best aid there is; and if you cannot, then have him moved according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, where some substance leaks out of it, or the skin is swollen where one can see or feel it clearly:
