car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the threads are thick, as I have seen foolish people make their bandages out of twisted coarse flaxen cords, and this is a great error, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should not be more than two fibers' width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is raw under the splints after the dislocation, then put beneath them flax or lambswool, so that it does not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the hernia is broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should not extract all the broken bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	Because when a limb is large, one should not put splints on it until after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on the heat of the abscess;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and here is the method of ancient splints for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: You should take flour that is ground at the mill and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method of the splint that restores fractures in many ways, especially in women and small children, because it is not too cold or too hot.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster that restores broken bones and dislocation and twisting: take 3 parts each of elderberries, ladanums, aniseed and asafoetida, and gum arabic; myrrh and aloes, each 5 parts; alechi 8 parts; grind them into powder and mix with egg white. If the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it restores broken bones until they heal, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is good for twisting: take myrrh and viscud, each 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, each 8 parts; açai berry 6 parts; Armenian bole 10 parts, and grind well, and cook in water or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of plaster for joints and dislocated bones: take a new lamb's wool, moisten it in lard and cooked oil, and apply it to the affected area. This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and removing pain. It also smooths out bumps on the bones and reduces swelling.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and deadnettle leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster out of it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of bone fracture and to reduce the swelling of the abscess. Take the root of comfrey, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, each one part; and grind, and cook with wine, and if the member is inflamed, cook with coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of plaster that is stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member. Take the roots of comfrey, and flax seed, fennel, milk thistle, and blackthorn, and violet flowers and chamomile, each one part; and grind, and cook with salt water or sweet water, or wine, depending on the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypochares says in his book that one should not put anything on the broken member except to restore it with a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it be kept between two things, neither too soft nor too hard.Quant l’homme ou la feme est prestes a la mort, et sent le corps fraich et colde, et ne se remue plus, prene une foye et li foyez les culles, et le cul de la foye metez sus li petiz orifices qui sont en haut li corps, si com est entre li coudes, sus li poilz de la teste, sus li petiz orifices qui sont pres l’ombelice; et les culles li metes sus li petiz orifices qui sont pres li codres.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen says that one should put on the broken member, to restore it, dry things that are slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense, and similar things, as we have said.Quant l’homme ou la feme est prestes a la mort, et sent le corps fraich et colde, et ne se remue plus, prene une foye et li foyez les culles, et le cul de la foye metez sus li petiz orifices qui sont en haut li corps, si com est entre li coudes, sus li poilz de la teste, sus li petiz orifices qui sont pres l’ombelice; et les culles li metes sus li petiz orifices qui sont pres li codres.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of ointment that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and human hair, or bird feathers, and bee's wax, and mix them together, and grind them, and make an ointment from it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen it a little after, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor move the bone from its place; if so, do not loosen it for several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching comes to the area, or discomfort or swelling, then act quickly and loosen it, and remove the ointment immediately; and take a light cloth, and a sponge of sea moss, and dip it in water, and apply it to the area until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then place it on a dry bed, moistened with water or rose oil, and cover it with a cloth, until you are sure there is no hot abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and relieve the inflammation in the limb, and remove the pain, then restart the gentle massage, and use a little ointment, and do not pull as hard as before; gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, and you need ointment and bandages, then restart it, just as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said happens to the limb, do not remove it for 3, 4, 5, or 7 days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals and the bone approaches the flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then reduce it more than before, and increase the meat, as I said earlier; and if you see the site drying out more than necessary, know that nutrition cannot reach it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	arise from hot water, every time you release it, and this is each third day, and loosen a little the bandage.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	through this work thus the healing reaches the limb, and gradually improves that which the foolish do, who restore the limb crookedly: it is bad, and such work is cowardly, and I see nothing else than weariness and doing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, with different shapes, and the causes are varied.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for it has fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, and the collar bone is broken all the way to the shoulder blade which is under the bone, as in an axe or pole; and because of this, this type of fracture is called "axe fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "surface fracture"; and the wound from these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a concussive impact, or a cleaving or collar-bone fracture from stone, or from falling on stone, or other similar injuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture which approaches the membrane under the bone, or it is on top of the bone; and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound which is lodged in the bone as subtly as a hair, and the split is small, and for this reason this fracture is called 'capillary'.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by a stone or by falling or by similar means, and drives the bone below, and the site is hairy like the blacksmiths when they work on the anvils; then the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones in their heads, such as children's heads;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it happens in all these ways of breaking that fine pieces are dislocated as if they were tiles; and I will speak about this later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the distraction over them, and the interrogation under a tent, and through the corruption of the flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is discovered when one uncovers the bone and rubs it, and a black line appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be careful of bad omens from the patient, and if you see any harmful signs, such as vomiting blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, fever, eyes popping out, or similar signs in various conditions, then they cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you don't see any frightening signs and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the newborn comes to you first, and it is winter, you should remove the foreskin before the fourteenth day when you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the spring, you should remove the foreskin before the seventh day so that the skin under the foreskin does not rot and the complications we have mentioned arise.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone extends just to the membrane that covers the brain, then you should split the damaged part thus: and you must hold the head of the injured person firmly, and expose the bone in all the ways you can, and as deeply as you can into the wound,
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone, or a pus-filled abscess, then assist with whatever is appropriate, and fill the wound with soft rags soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	let the wound rest until the hot abscess is soothed and you are sure there is no bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways of operating. The first way is that you cut a close fit in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then [you cut] another slit larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various cuts, some narrow and some wide, and they are pointed and made of iron; and work gently so that you do not bleeding the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, you must pierce it all around, so that you apply cuts with chisels, not so deep that they go through the bone, and you should have a rim or circle on top, preventing the point from going through the bone; and you should have several of these, so that each one comes in the thickness of the bone, so that you have chisels for all parts of the head. And this is the shape of the 3 types of chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place a probe on the bone and move it with your fingers until you know the bone is pierced; then move the probe elsewhere a little later, and do this all around; then cut into the space between the bones with your incision tools as subtly and lightly as you can, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or with one of the instruments you have, like tweezers or pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and drawn the bone, it is appropriate that you resect the sharp edge that remains on the bone with any suitable instrument like an incision tool, but it should be more slender and sharper than the other incision tools.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	If anything remains of the small bones or any chips, remove them gently with one of your tools; then treat the wound with tenting and poultices as we have described.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment, which Galen describes and highly recommends, is as follows:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First you must uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you place under it the head of this lens-shaped instrument, which has this shape.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut on one side, but the part is jagged in .ij. sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then hit gently with a small mallet, so that you carefully strike the bone all around, and be careful of the membrane underneath it.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is attached to the bone, then loosen it gently, because one can loosen it well without harm and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce all the way to the membrane, and it is only cut slightly on top, and there are small pieces, then one must smooth out that roughness, and remove the scales with a very subtle rasp; one must have various sizes according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use a large razor at first, then one that is more delicate, and do not stop doing this until it is good.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-cutting and shaving techniques, you must adapt to the individual, and this is something that cannot be taught to one who has not devoted themselves to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is exposed, you should place a linen bandage, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it over the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another bandage that is doubled over two or three times, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first bandage; and do this as gently as you can so that you do not put too much pressure on the wound, then apply another ligature above it, and do not tighten it more than is necessary to hold the wound;
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and let it stay like that for one or two days, until the abscess is soothed, then loosen it and apply remedies such as lily roots, wheat flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things. Make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and then apply other remedies without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and ensure that the wound is clean before you leave off the ointment and do not allow any pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the brain's membrane, it hardens and causes great harm to the patient. When one applies something biting to a wound, it bites into the flesh.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care therefore, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come but because of the medicine one has put on it, that such virtue has, you must take a part of honey and mix with it three parts of rose oil and mix them into a paste, and place it on the wound;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat him with appropriate treatments until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose are broken, one only, for there are two bones; and below is cartilage, which does not break, but only swells or becomes dislocated, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should put your little finger or a probe into the nose, and push the broken part back into place with your index finger, and hold it there until the nose returns to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the teeth, and the jaw cannot reach its place, then you should put it equal to the head of a rather thick rod.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, do likewise, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot abscesses are appeased, then attach to the head of the jaw tenters of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you attach one to another side, if the fracture is there; and let the tenters be so thick that they fill the holes of the jaw.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some restorer said that one must wet the bandages with butter and change them every day. It seems to me that this is not good, but they should be wet in preparation of egg yolk and mill powder; then leave the bandage, until the bone is set and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers of geese are put in place of bandages, and over this a silk cloth is wound around, and the fracture is bound tightly, and the patient breathes through it; now do as you will.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come to the ears while you are working there, then put cerate or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a poultice of diaquilone.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if hot abscesses do not come, then put on a warm poultice of flour of sisamen and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk, then put over it light sponges, but do not bandage the ears.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture of the bone is small and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with appropriate tools for that purpose, then close the wound and treat it with healing, warming poultices and ointments suitable for that purpose.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the bone, then treat it with tents and insert splinters of wood until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Regarding the dislocation of the jaw:
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated beneath and there is no external wound, and the dislocation is only slight without any fracture, they can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, to put your left index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, put your right index finger, and gently push the fracture inside, and make it even with the other hand by force.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is displaced in [one of two places], then you must administer extension in one part, so that it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth, or splitting, then they must be restrained with a thread of gold or silver or silk; then put a cerote on the broken jaw, and place upon it a double piece of cloth; and upon the cloth, place a large well-made splint, or a piece of leather of equal length and width according to the jaw, and bind it in place as tightly as you can; and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the shape is changing, then loosen it on the third day, and then put back into place what has changed; and apply a poultice over it, made of powdered millstone with an abundance of egg or flour of salsify, after you have removed the cerote; and upon the poultice, apply a thin layer of lamb's wool, and if the poultices become soiled, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it takes for him to recover; many times recovery takes place within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses arise, then administer what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, examine whether any piece of bone has been removed; then remove it subtly with suitable instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, then sew up the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it suitable poultices to encourage scabs, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks in several ways in front of the shoulder, and the break is according to three patterns: it can be broken and separated into two pieces, which is the easiest to restore; or there can be a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is as follows when the break is without a wound: you need two assistants, one of whom holds the shoulder where the forceps are broken, and the other stretches the neck towards the affected part; then, with your fingers, bring the broken pieces together so that the joint is in the correct position, with no visible gap or misalignment.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you need to extend the joint further, place a round pillow of cloth or fabric under the shoulder, and make it as thick as necessary; then release the forceps and hold the pillow in your hand, bringing the broken pieces together so that they are aligned correctly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder out of its socket because it comes in deeply, then the patient should lie on his back, and put one ear to the ground, and the minister should push the shoulder down while lifting the bone of the shoulder.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then you should apply the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it broken, then you must split it; gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot join because of an overgrowth, then cut it at one of the incisions you have made; but put this instrument under the shoulder to ward off the syphilis:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and is shaped like a spoon, but not flat, and is as wide as it needs to be according to the size of the bone and the extent of the wound; and has two handles, one wide and the other narrow, depending on the shape of the incision you made when you pulled the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the incision is small, or if you doubt the hot abscess, then pack the wound with bandages and tents according to its amount.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if there are deep abscesses, moisten a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The dislocation of a bone, when there is no wound or cut, is to apply the powder of the mill and egg white, and put light dressings on top, and place a splint underneath if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide band of cloth about the width of a palm, then put a double layer of cloth over the dressings and plaster; next take a thin strip of wood about six inches long and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the strip over the fracture, and wind the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the affected armpit; and adjust it from each end, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture in alignment, and you clearly see that the strip does not move over the broken bone, then release it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	let the patient lie on his back and place a small pillow under his shoulder to raise the shoulder joint; thus the fracture of the collar bone will be relieved by the alignment of the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck and do not untie it unless some mishap occurs, for up to 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then start the poultice again if you see that it is needed, and leave it on until it is healed; usually it takes 28 days to heal, but some people recover in less time.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It can happen that the shoulder is broken or displaced, and it does not hurt when touched; then adjust it according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way you can. Then apply powdered flour with egg white, and light gauze, and place it on a double piece of cloth; then place it over a wide and thin stone, which is slightly larger than the shoulder. If there are bumps underneath the stone on the shoulder, then cover those bumps with gauze so that the stone sits evenly. Then bind it tightly with a large bandage, so that the stone does not move from its position, and check the binding every day; and each time it becomes loose, tighten it again, and adjust the stone if it has moved out of place. Let the patient lie on his side, and the shoulder will be healed in 20 to 25 days. When these number of days are complete, then remove the bandage, and be careful, for it is not a bone that heals easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward, and not under the heart, they should cut it off, and the bone, and do what we have said about relieving the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the break in the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but that rarely happens; it is more often broken on the top. And when it is broken in the middle, it declines towards the bottom, and the patient feels great pain and loss of strength, and becomes weak all over, and may vomit blood, and the wound opens in the broken bone, which feels very painful.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is for the patient to lie on his back, and place a pillow between his shoulders, then press the shoulders together and bring the ribs close together with his hands, making sure that the bones are in their proper position; then he should apply plasters and bandages over the broken bone, using salt or some other light material, and wrap it in a cloth, binding it firmly to the bone so that it does not move; then he should bind the linen tightly around the waist, and every hour loosen the binding, and if it softens, tighten it again; and if it needs to be loosed for corrosion or itching that comes to the area, or pain or abscess, then he should hurry and loosen it, and wash away what has come out from the wound, and dress it according to the various methods of treatment; then re-apply the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures occur only in the large ribs near the back, and in the upper part inside, and they bend only because they are slippery; and one feels it well on examination at both ends.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the treatment is that you put it back in place, as it should be. And then apply the ointment, and hold it steady with a bandage, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is bent inward, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, as with pleurisy, for the bone punctures the lining; and he has difficulty breathing, and coughs up a great quantity of blood, and it is a serious illness, and the ancient physicians placed great importance on it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if one has a fracture, they say that one should eat foods that bloat the belly, to force out the broken bone.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make hot poultices unless an abscess is already there.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it is there, then we cleanse it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should place leeches on the site to draw out pus, and this is reasonable; however, there is a risk that the leech will attract excess fluids due to the weakness of the patient.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the place with soft wool soaked in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the area around even, then it should be bandaged with a bandage of pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear due to the bone pointing through the bandage, and there is doubt about the patient, then one should split above the site of the broken rib, and place an instrument underneath to ward off the infection; and then one should cut the bone and gently pull, and then sew the two lips of the wound if it is large, and bandage it with poultices until it heals. And if hot abscesses arise, then place moistened fabrics in rose oil on the site, and while treating the area where the abscess is, let the patient lie carefully on his side, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	about the fracture of the neck:
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and it can bend; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will recover or not, pay attention to whether his hands are soft and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them or straighten them, and when you prick him with a needle, he does not feel it. Know that he is mortally ill in many conditions, and if he is mute and feels well when one presses and pricks him, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the ailment will be cured if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if a similar condition occurs in the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will recover or not, pay attention to whether his feet are soft, and whether the signs are in his hands, and there is windiness and urination without willing it; and when he is pressed on his belly, there is urination without willing it. And when he is pressed on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot. Know that he is mortally ill: do not labor in his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these signs do not occur, the condition is more mild.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply a hot poultice to the spine if there is an abscess, using rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is soothed; then apply one of the comforting and drying poultices, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, one should cover it with the palm of one's hand; and remove the bone, then join the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a single stitch, then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the 'head of the cow', put your thumb in your left hand, and place it equally in your right hand, then apply the plaster and bandage on top, if you need to; then bind it tightly, and if there are bones dislocated, do the same, then remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes the hip bone is fractured, and if it does, there will be a slight shrinking at the head; and it will bend to one side, and the patient feels pain in that spot, and there will be a point and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And its restoration is that you extend your hand over it, so that you are on the fracture; and you know which is the fracture and the shape of it; and if the fracture is only at the head, then put that fracture in line with the rest of the bone so that it is in a natural shape.Et si la brisure est au pardedens soulement, si met cele sus le chief tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it inclines inward, then have the patient lie on his stomach until the setting of that fracture is prepared.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, then apply the plaster, and then place a wooden or leather splint on top, and bind the fracture so that it does not move; and apply the linen under the rib cage until the fracture is healed.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if painful bumps appear, do not touch them until the painful bumps are soothed, and apply what we have described earlier; then return to the healing process, and bind it as it should be, if there is no bad outcome; and that is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires is that which is between the neck and the head of the shoulder; and if it is broken, one should restore it according to one of two methods. The first is that you take a rod straight and smooth, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with ropes and raise them up, and seat the patient on a chair; then let him gently hang his broken arm over the rod, until it comes to rest, and have a curve in the rod, then let him lean back onto something heavy or let his ministers hold him down; then let his assistants bring the broken joint together as evenly as possible, so that the joint returns to its proper place.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on his back, and ties his hand to his neck, then let one minister hold what is above the break in his hands, and the other minister hold below at the end of the rod, and each pulls their respective ends.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then press down on one side under the fracture and up on the other, and stretch each of the joints in their direction. And if the fracture is near the top of the shoulder, then you should put a light bandage underneath the shoulder pad, and another towards the neck, under the fracture; and also, if the fracture is towards the neck, a light bandage should be placed gently without labor, so that the fracture is even both in place and on the neck; then adjust the fracture as it should be, and press it, if no hot abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if hot abscesses come, do not tighten it for 7 days; then put cool linen in vinegar and rose oil on the hot abscesses until they are soothed; then tighten it, and the manner of tightening is that you put the plaster on the fracture, then raise the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put a cloth, and press onto the shoulder and the arm so that the arm is in its natural place, unless something keeps it from being so, or if the bone is displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use splints, and put a wider and stronger splint on the fracture, with a space of two fingers between each splint, and let each splint be as long so that it passes the fracture by three inches on each side; then tighten onto the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter, more firmly and less in moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the seating of the stars, and the constriction, as we have said, at the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, let it lie bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the binding every three days, so that itching nor swelling come to the spot, nor the growth come to the member because it is too tight. Then release it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents come, then unbind it after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put underneath the shoulder one cushion full of wool equally, and look every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken member does not move, nor the binding become soft; then release it by the power of medicine, and give him the food we have previously mentioned, so that the food is in the first subtleties; and when he begins to recover, let the food be thick. It is customary for the shoulder and arm to be healed within 40 days; then one should unbind it and administer baths and medicines of ointments to heal the spot. And if the constriction is bad and swollen, let it remain bound for 1 or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "bone-pair"; one is small and lies beneath the armpit, and the other is large and lies beneath the small bone; sometimes only the large bone breaks, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When only the small bone is broken, its restoration and healing are easy; but when only the large bone is broken, healing is more difficult and painful than when both are broken together. If it is only the small bone that is broken, then one should gently extend and straighten it.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone, then one must pull harder; and extend the arm on .1. cushion, and raise the armpit of the hand higher than the other, and the small bones lower than the other bones, and have the patient cross his arms over his chest, and place .1. cushion in front of him so that he does not suffer any strain; then extend the minister's arm above the part under his hand, or to .1. ligament, and another minister at .1. the other above. Then one should straighten the member according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breaking there are pieces, one places each in its place, and if there is any dislocation that pinches the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then split it along the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken singularly about it in this chapter; then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if at the beginning of restoration, abscesses occur, then apply a dressing of cerote made from rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and lay a dress over it subtly, until the hot abscess is relieved. And then remove the cerote, and apply the plaster of mill-powder with egg albumen, then put on the bandages, and let the bandage over the fracture be a little stronger and larger than the others; and understand that he must have six bandages on his arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and tighten more over the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as time goes by, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the dressings over the fracture be soft and moist, not hard or dry; and let the thread with which he is being bound be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And change the bandages and the sling after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accident happens to the member, such as itching that comes on it, then you must wet the member with warm water until those itches are relieved; and let the member not be bound but rest. And then resume the binding, and if the bandages are softened and the bones separated, and anything like that, then dress it again.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you see that the nourishment cannot come to the member because it is too bound, then you must soften it a little, and leave it thus for several days, until the nourishment runs to it, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not release him until twenty days have passed; then let him keep his hands on his neck, and let his neck remain even, and guard against movement and agitation, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is healed in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the composition and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and around the fingers there are few fractures, and they only come from bending many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, then the patient should stretch his arm out straight in front of him evenly; then he should put his hand on the ground, and stretch out the broken bones, and put them back together evenly, the minister, as far as the injury extends; and if there are no abscesses, then put on a plaster and bandages; then wrap it in a single linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the peritoneum around the abdomen of the plant, make a bandage of rags, and instruct the patient to press it against his broken plant; then squeeze it with a long strip of cloth, and let the mark of the finger be as large as the palm of the hand, and squeeze it as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the arm, you must put a splint on top and another underneath in the plant, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand and stop the bleeding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture is in one of the fingers, if it's the thumb, set it straight as it should be and then squeeze the hand, and if you see fit, put a small straight splint to raise the fracture and keep it from moving; and if the fracture is in any other finger, such as the index or another, set it straight and bind it with the finger next to it; or bind them all together while holding it steady, or you can put a splint on top of the finger like a thumb; take care in the restoration and treatment of a hot abscess, and treat any pus that arises as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken, and one can see this when they bend forward and backward; and their healing is by binding one band above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And let the patient lie on his face, then extend each band equally to their respective parts; and this is how it is done when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, then one band should be towards the buttock, and the other band below the fracture. And likewise, if it is near the knee, then the band should be beyond the knee, and the extension should be downward; then place the splints so that the bone is aligned with its natural shape, and then apply the poultice and the bandage, unless an abscess forms.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if the patient has a hot abscess, then let it subside and then return to your treatment and care; the bandage is done in the following way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap a bandage around the fracture, a thick one folded in half or two layers, and leave it loose, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the base of the nail, and thread a long piece of string between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and let the end of the string come up above; then turn the bandage over the leg and thigh, then put splints on the fracture, and put one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to make the binding even, then start to tie it firmly in three or four places around the fracture; as you go higher above the fracture, make the binding looser; then take hold of the two ends of the string that you have threaded between the leg and the thigh, and tie the three splints that are on top, then go back down to the end of the string, so that it comes under the foot; tighten it so that it doesn't move from its place, then leave it like that until any swelling or bruising goes down and no new ones appear.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if something happens, then loosen it and adjust what has happened, as we have said many times before; and if there are pieces of bone that are poking out, they should be removed if possible; if not, the area should be split open and drained, and the wound treated as we have described, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Sometimes the thigh is broken like this when splints are put on, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, when restored in this way, it does not harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you should know that the neck is restored within a day, or less or more, depending on the different complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	You should know that in the groove of the knee there is little breaking, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is only a split, or an opening, and it happens with all wounds, and without wounds, and this feels good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put it back in place with tweezers, as long as he can; then put on the ointment, and if necessary, put a round splint, and bind it as it should be, then follow all the instructions that we have given for other fractures, such as a hot abscess and similar; then treat each incident as appropriate, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	You should know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is properly called the "mustelz" and the other the "foscile"; and all manner of fractures occur as they do in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as for the arm, and the procedures are the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns completely inside out.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if only the smaller bones are broken, then it turns forward.
